# Consultation 65 — Phase 4: docs validation

Phase 3 landed dual-green at commit `df24e17`. Phase 4 is the
public-facing documentation set that plugin authors will build
against. The user explicitly asked for the docs to be **very
descriptive and accurate and validated with the triad** — they
intend to build a test plugin against these docs from another
project, so accuracy is the gate.

## Files to review

1. `docs/integration-guide.md` — the main onboarding document.
   ~470 lines. Plugin authors read this end-to-end.
2. `docs/crypto-spec.md` — the canonical V1 crypto contract.
   ~330 lines. Other implementations (server, Android, SDKs)
   must agree byte-for-byte.
3. `docs/ROADMAP.md` — public roadmap. ~52 lines. Sets
   expectations on what's shipped vs forthcoming.

## What changed in Phase 4

### integration-guide.md
- **§1 "What you're building"** — rewritten to introduce the two
  renderer modes (`script` / `template`) and two card types
  (`event` / `live`) up front, so readers know which combination
  they want before reading further.
- **"What the host does for you"** — added live-card pinning
  rule, cross-device dismiss filter, SSE / FCM hint channel.
- **§5.1 Native Template Renderer** — expanded the stub into a
  full section: a working `publish_plugin(...)` example with
  `renderer="template"`, the JSONPath dialect rules, the
  `standard_card` layout's required-and-allowed fields, the
  action-POST contract (host posts the full decrypted payload,
  no Authorization header), and the publish-time validator rules
  with explicit 422 trigger conditions.
- **§5.2 Live Cards** — expanded the stub: full
  `publish_plugin(..., card_type="live", card_key_path="$.x")`
  example, a complete `upsert_card(...)` example showing where
  the live-card AAD comes from, and an explicit table of the
  4xx gates the server enforces on upsert (pairing, plugin
  active, TTL window, sequence monotonicity, rate limit). The
  `delete_card` example now passes `user_id` (consultation 62
  RED #5 security fix is now exposed in the public API surface).
- **§7 Action callback** — split into a script-renderer path
  (plugin builds the body via `platform.network.fetch`) and a
  template-renderer path (host POSTs the full decrypted payload
  verbatim with no Authorization header — the security-boundary
  invariant from consultation 62 RED #1 is now documented).
- **§8 Testing** — replaced the stale "15s poll" line with the
  SSE flow + FCM background fallback.
- **§9 Common errors** — added Phase 3b card-upsert errors
  (410/400/409 per the consultation 63 router-mapping fixes).

### crypto-spec.md
- **§8 Live Cards** added: the AAD shape (7 fields, integer
  `sequence_number`, `Z` suffix on ISO timestamps), upsert
  envelope canonical JSON, delete envelope canonical JSON. The
  delete envelope explicitly requires `user_id` and documents
  *why* (the cross-user-delete vulnerability from consultation
  62 RED #5).
- Python reference snippets at the bottom now include
  `assemble_live_card_aad`, `assemble_live_card_upsert_envelope`,
  `assemble_live_card_delete_envelope` so other SDK authors can
  copy-paste an authoritative canonical-bytes builder.

### ROADMAP.md
- Replaced the confusing "Phase 4 / 5 / 6 / 7 / 8" labeling
  (which collided with the internal implementation phases used
  in consultations) with **V1 / V1.5 / V2 / V3 / V4** version
  milestones. V1 is the shipped state (matches commit
  `df24e17`); the others are sequenced by platform dependency.
- Top of the file explicitly distinguishes the public
  roadmap-versioning from the internal implementation phases
  tracked in `.triad/50-agreement-and-plan.md`, so future
  readers can map between the two if they need to.

## What I need from each reviewer

1. **Accuracy against the code.** For every API signature,
   error code, JSON shape, or HTTP status documented in the
   guide, confirm the code at `df24e17` matches. Specifically:
   - `client.publish_plugin(...)` keyword arguments + defaults.
   - `client.upsert_card(...)` keyword arguments + defaults
     (including server-enforced 48h cap, 1/sec rate limit, the
     409 sequence-regression status).
   - `client.delete_card(...)` requires `user_id` (Codex 62 RED
     #5 fix).
   - `client.send_to(...)` payload shape + `hostPreview` caps.
   - `client.revoke_plugin(...)` reason enum + UX descriptions.
   - Phase 3b error codes (410 plugin not live / no pairing,
     400 TTL, 409 sequence) are the codes the router actually
     returns after the consultation 63 mapping fix.
   - SSE event types in the §1 "what the host does for you"
     block match what `EventStreamManager` parses.

2. **Crypto canonical bytes.** Confirm the live-card AAD shape
   in `crypto-spec.md §8.1` byte-for-byte matches:
   - `android/core/crypto/.../Aad.kt:62 LiveCardAad`.
   - `sdk-python/syncler/crypto.py` (if it has a live-card
     helper) or the inline construction in the live-card SDK
     methods.
   - The server's `assemble_envelope({...})` invocations in
     `app/routers/cards.py` for upsert and delete envelopes.
   Specifically: `sequence_number` is an integer literal in
   JSON (no quotes); `expires_at` uses `Z` suffix not `+00:00`;
   UUIDs are lowercase no-brace form before signing.

3. **Plugin-author buildability.** Could a developer who has
   never seen this codebase build a working **template-renderer
   live-card** plugin from these docs alone? List the gaps. Be
   ruthless — if a step needs guessing, it's a doc bug.

4. **Security-relevant statements.** Verify the docs correctly
   describe:
   - The host explicitly NOT attaching `Authorization` to
     template-renderer action POSTs (the §1 paragraph + §5.1
     bullet + §7 paragraph all need to agree).
   - The user-id binding in the delete envelope.
   - The server-enforced 48h TTL cap (not caller-controlled).
   - The publish-time validator rules for template manifests.

5. **Anything missing.** Plugin lifecycle gaps, common error
   conditions not covered, security caveats the docs gloss
   over, pricing/quota considerations the platform doesn't yet
   document.

## Output

Per reviewer:
1. Per-file verdict: GREEN / YELLOW / RED with specific
   doc-line references for any non-GREEN.
2. Specific code-vs-doc mismatches with file:line citations on
   both sides.
3. Specific buildability gaps a plugin author would hit.
4. Overall: ready to commit / ready after fixes / hold.

If both reviewers GREEN, Phase 4 commits as-is and the user has
their public-contract documentation set. If either flags
accuracy issues, fix and re-fire.

docs/ROADMAP.md:43:15. **Per-plugin user preferences.** Notification cadence, label overrides, delivery-window scheduling, do-not-disturb integration — all surfaced from the host's settings sheet without plugin-side code.
docs/integration-guide.md:5:Syncler does not know what your data looks like, what your UI says, or what your buttons do. Your payload, your plugin code (or template manifest), your callback endpoint — Syncler just routes bytes.
docs/integration-guide.md:12:- **Template** (`renderer: "template"`) — no JavaScript. You ship a small JSON manifest that maps fields out of your payload via JSONPath (`$.title`, `$.body.summary`) into a native Material 3 card. Buttons are host-rendered and the host POSTs the decrypted payload to the action's declared endpoint. Faster, lighter, no JS attack surface; constrained to a fixed set of layouts.
docs/integration-guide.md:14:And one of two delivery modes:
docs/integration-guide.md:16:- **Event** (`card_type: "event"`) — the default. Each `send_to` produces a new immutable inbox row. Good for notifications, alerts, transactional events.
docs/integration-guide.md:17:- **Live** (`card_type: "live"`) — persistent, upsertable. Subsequent upserts to the same `card_key` replace the previous payload (highest `sequence_number` wins). Good for status cards that change over time (delivery progress, market position, sensor reading). Server-enforced 48h TTL; you re-upsert to extend.
docs/integration-guide.md:21:The Syncler inbox shows a *native* row for every message — sender name, title, subtitle, summary, arrival time — pulled from the `hostPreview` block you embed in your payload (§2). The detail view that opens on tap is what your script bundle's `render()` or your template manifest produces.
docs/integration-guide.md:27:- **Native row rendering** from your `hostPreview` block (title / subtitle / summary) plus the server's arrival time (HH:mm for today, MMM d for older).
docs/integration-guide.md:30:- **Inbox search** (case-insensitive substring) over title, subtitle, summary, sender name, AND any tokens you supplied in `hostPreview.searchText`.
docs/integration-guide.md:35:- **Live cards pin above events.** When mixed in the same inbox, live cards (`card_type: "live"`) sort above event cards (`card_type: "event"`), each subsorted by recency. The "Live" view in the drawer shows only live cards.
docs/integration-guide.md:36:- **Cross-device dismiss.** When the user dismisses a message on device A, the server marks `DeliveryStatus.dismissed_at` for that device. Device B's next inbox pull (driven by the `dismiss` SSE event or a fresh refresh) excludes the dismissed row — `inbox_for_device` LEFT JOINs `DeliveryStatus` and filters `dismissed_at IS NULL`. Per-device dismiss, server-side.
docs/integration-guide.md:37:- **Real-time hints over SSE.** Foreground devices keep an authenticated Server-Sent Events stream open to `/v1/events`. The server pushes content-blind hints — `inbox.changed`, `state.changed`, `dismiss`, `card.upsert`, `card.delete` — and the client re-fetches over REST in response. The actual payloads still flow over the existing pull endpoints; SSE is the wakeup signal, not the data channel. Backgrounded devices fall back to FCM.
docs/integration-guide.md:39:You don't need to opt into any of these. Populate `hostPreview` and they all work.

docs/integration-guide.md:434:**Template renderer** — the host POSTs the **full decrypted payload** as the body, verbatim. There's no JS hook to intervene. Your endpoint receives the whole payload JSON; pull whatever fields you need server-side. No `Authorization` header is added by the host (the user's Syncler bearer token never reaches your endpoint — security boundary). If you need request authentication, HMAC the payload using a sender-specific secret your backend shares out of band with itself, or rely on TLS + endpoint allowlisting alone.
docs/integration-guide.md:436:Note: the platform does **not** inject `device_id` into the body for you in V1. If you need to distinguish which device acted, include a sender-generated identifier in your payload and (for script renderer) have the plugin echo it back. For template renderer, your `card_key` (or any other field in the payload) serves the same dedupe role. Dedupe by `item_id` / `card_key` alone if a single tap is what you care about.
docs/integration-guide.md:439:- Status 409 -> idempotent dedupe (already saw this item); platform may retry on transient network errors so be ready.

docs/integration-guide.md:464:8. The server pushes an `inbox.changed` event over the SSE stream the open app is subscribed to (foreground); the phone refreshes its inbox, decrypts the message, fetches your bundle (or applies your template manifest), and shows the native row within ~1s. If the app is backgrounded, FCM wakes it and the inbox refresh happens on the next foreground.
docs/integration-guide.md:471:- **`410 plugin missing, revoked, or not owned by sender`** — `plugin_id` (the row UUID) is wrong, or you accidentally used `plugin_identifier`. The two are distinct (see §5 vs §6).
docs/integration-guide.md:472:- **`410 recipient has no active devices`** — the user has no enrolled device (signed up but never opened the app, or revoked all devices). FCM availability is *not* required; messages are stored regardless and pulled via `/v1/messages/inbox`.
docs/integration-guide.md:473:- **`409 nonce already used`** — your code reused a nonce somehow; SDK generates fresh nonces per `send_to`, so this means you're calling `send_to` with cached envelope bytes. Rebuild.
docs/integration-guide.md:475:- **`410 plugin missing, revoked, not live-type, or not owned by sender`** (cards upsert) — the plugin row's `card_type` isn't `"live"`, or the row has a non-null `revoked_at`, or the publish row's `sender_id` doesn't match the signed envelope's sender. The error message is intentionally generic so a probing caller can't distinguish the cases (don't leak which plugin UUIDs exist).
docs/integration-guide.md:476:- **`410 no active pairing`** (cards upsert) — the recipient user has not paired with your sender, or the pairing has been revoked. The user needs to re-scan your pairing QR.
docs/integration-guide.md:477:- **`400 expires_at exceeds the 48h live-card cap`** (cards upsert) — your supplied `expires_at` is more than 48 hours from now. Live cards are capped server-side to prevent slot squatting. Send shorter and re-upsert to extend.
docs/integration-guide.md:478:- **`400 expires_at is not in the future`** (cards upsert) — you sent an already-expired `expires_at`. Use a future timestamp.
docs/integration-guide.md:479:- **`409 sequence_number not greater than existing`** (cards upsert) — the existing card has a `sequence_number` ≥ what you sent. Sequence must be strictly increasing per `card_key`.
docs/integration-guide.md:482:- **`HostPreviewValidationError: hostPreview.X is N UTF-8 bytes; max is M`** — caught at `client.send_to` time. Trim the offending field; see §2 for the caps. UTF-8 byte counts, not characters — emoji and accented characters cost more than one byte.
docs/integration-guide.md:483:- **Row shows "New message from {sender}" with fallback text only** — your message was sent without a `hostPreview` block, or the block was malformed (logged + ignored on the device). The detail view still loads the plugin and renders normally; only the row is generic. Add a valid `hostPreview` and re-send.
docs/integration-guide.md:489:Publish every plugin release as a new row under the same `plugin_identifier`. `plugin_identifier` is the stable name, while `plugin_row_id` is the exact version row returned by `client.publish_plugin(...)`.
docs/integration-guide.md:503:1. **Revoke the device**: Go to **Settings -> Devices** on a trusted device and revoke the lost one. This immediately kills its network access and SSE stream.

docs/crypto-spec.md:240:`card_type` is always the string `"live"` (the field exists so the AAD shape can extend cleanly when future card types land — e.g. ephemeral or scheduled cards). `sequence_number` is emitted as a JSON integer literal (no quotes); senders MUST NOT stringify it. `expires_at` MUST use the `Z` UTC suffix (not `+00:00`) so SDK and server agree on the canonical bytes.
docs/crypto-spec.md:242:The AAD binds the ciphertext to a specific (sender, user, plugin, card, sequence, expiry) tuple. A replay of an older sequence or a substitution of one card's ciphertext under another's metadata will fail AES-GCM tag verification on decrypt.
docs/crypto-spec.md:251:  "card_type": "live",
docs/crypto-spec.md:257:  "sequence_number": <integer JSON literal>,
docs/crypto-spec.md:276:**`user_id` is REQUIRED in the envelope.** Without it, a delete signature valid for one user's card could be replayed against another user's card with a coincidentally matching `(sender_id, card_key)` — the table is uniquely keyed on `(sender_id, user_id, card_key)`, so the lookup would otherwise be ambiguous. (Codex consultation 62 security finding.) The server matches the exact triple before deleting; mismatched triples no-op silently and still publish a `card.delete` SSE event so all of the user's devices clear any stale local copy.
docs/crypto-spec.md:280:Live-card vectors live alongside the rest in `server/tests/test_crypto.py` (round-trip) and `android/core/crypto/.../SpecVectorsTest.kt` (Android cross-check). The canonical envelope bytes for upsert/delete are asserted in `server/tests/test_phase3.py` via signature-verification round trips against `app/routers/cards.py:_build_upsert_envelope_bytes` and `_build_delete_envelope_bytes`.

.\docs\crypto-spec.md:231:  "card_type": "live",
.\docs\crypto-spec.md:240:`card_type` is always the string `"live"` (the field exists so the AAD shape can extend cleanly when future card types land — e.g. ephemeral or scheduled cards). `sequence_number` is emitted as a JSON integer literal (no quotes); senders MUST NOT stringify it. `expires_at` MUST use the `Z` UTC suffix (not `+00:00`) so SDK and server agree on the canonical bytes.
.\docs\crypto-spec.md:251:  "card_type": "live",
.\docs\crypto-spec.md:262:The server constructs the same canonical bytes from the request body (via `assemble_envelope` in `server/app/routers/cards.py`) and verifies against the registered sender's public key. UUIDs MUST be canonicalized to lowercase no-brace form before signing (`str(uuid.UUID(value))`) — the SDK normalizes via `_canon_uuid` to prevent sender-side self-401s on uppercase or braced input.
.\docs\crypto-spec.md:276:**`user_id` is REQUIRED in the envelope.** Without it, a delete signature valid for one user's card could be replayed against another user's card with a coincidentally matching `(sender_id, card_key)` — the table is uniquely keyed on `(sender_id, user_id, card_key)`, so the lookup would otherwise be ambiguous. (Codex consultation 62 security finding.) The server matches the exact triple before deleting; mismatched triples no-op silently and still publish a `card.delete` SSE event so all of the user's devices clear any stale local copy.

.\docs\integration-guide.md:11:- **Script** (`renderer: "script"`) — a JavaScript bundle running inside a sandboxed WebView. Maximum flexibility; you ship a `render(payload)` function that returns HTML. Buttons POST through `platform.network.fetch`.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:12:- **Template** (`renderer: "template"`) — no JavaScript. You ship a small JSON manifest that maps fields out of your payload via JSONPath (`$.title`, `$.body.summary`) into a native Material 3 card. Buttons are host-rendered and the host POSTs the decrypted payload to the action's declared endpoint. Faster, lighter, no JS attack surface; constrained to a fixed set of layouts.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:16:- **Event** (`card_type: "event"`) — the default. Each `send_to` produces a new immutable inbox row. Good for notifications, alerts, transactional events.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:17:- **Live** (`card_type: "live"`) — persistent, upsertable. Subsequent upserts to the same `card_key` replace the previous payload (highest `sequence_number` wins). Good for status cards that change over time (delivery progress, market position, sensor reading). Server-enforced 48h TTL; you re-upsert to extend.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:19:In every case you also need **backend code** that publishes the plugin once and sends payloads on demand, plus (for script renderer) an HTTP endpoint that receives the action callback.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:21:The Syncler inbox shows a *native* row for every message — sender name, title, subtitle, summary, arrival time — pulled from the `hostPreview` block you embed in your payload (§2). The detail view that opens on tap is what your script bundle's `render()` or your template manifest produces.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:27:- **Native row rendering** from your `hostPreview` block (title / subtitle / summary) plus the server's arrival time (HH:mm for today, MMM d for older).
.\docs\integration-guide.md:30:- **Inbox search** (case-insensitive substring) over title, subtitle, summary, sender name, AND any tokens you supplied in `hostPreview.searchText`.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:34:- **Revocation UX** — if you revoke a plugin version with a `compromised` reason, the host refuses to execute the bundle on the device and shows a security banner instead. See §5.5.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:35:- **Live cards pin above events.** When mixed in the same inbox, live cards (`card_type: "live"`) sort above event cards (`card_type: "event"`), each subsorted by recency. The "Live" view in the drawer shows only live cards.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:36:- **Cross-device dismiss.** When the user dismisses a message on device A, the server marks `DeliveryStatus.dismissed_at` for that device. Device B's next inbox pull (driven by the `dismiss` SSE event or a fresh refresh) excludes the dismissed row — `inbox_for_device` LEFT JOINs `DeliveryStatus` and filters `dismissed_at IS NULL`. Per-device dismiss, server-side.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:37:- **Real-time hints over SSE.** Foreground devices keep an authenticated Server-Sent Events stream open to `/v1/events`. The server pushes content-blind hints — `inbox.changed`, `state.changed`, `dismiss`, `card.upsert`, `card.delete` — and the client re-fetches over REST in response. The actual payloads still flow over the existing pull endpoints; SSE is the wakeup signal, not the data channel. Backgrounded devices fall back to FCM.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:39:You don't need to opt into any of these. Populate `hostPreview` and they all work.

.\docs\integration-guide.md:392:The revoke request is signed by the SDK. The `reason` value is included in the signed envelope, so an intermediary cannot strip `compromised` down to a softer classification. Re-revoking a row keeps the original `revoked_at`; a higher-severity reason can promote the row, while downgrades are ignored.

.\docs\integration-guide.md:423:`https://your-app.example.com/api/action` accepts whatever body the host POSTs when the user taps an action button. The shape depends on which renderer you chose:
.\docs\integration-guide.md:425:**Script renderer** — your `onclick` handler builds the body via `platform.network.fetch`. In the §3 example that's:
.\docs\integration-guide.md:434:**Template renderer** — the host POSTs the **full decrypted payload** as the body, verbatim. There's no JS hook to intervene. Your endpoint receives the whole payload JSON; pull whatever fields you need server-side. No `Authorization` header is added by the host (the user's Syncler bearer token never reaches your endpoint — security boundary). If you need request authentication, HMAC the payload using a sender-specific secret your backend shares out of band with itself, or rely on TLS + endpoint allowlisting alone.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:436:Note: the platform does **not** inject `device_id` into the body for you in V1. If you need to distinguish which device acted, include a sender-generated identifier in your payload and (for script renderer) have the plugin echo it back. For template renderer, your `card_key` (or any other field in the payload) serves the same dedupe role. Dedupe by `item_id` / `card_key` alone if a single tap is what you care about.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:464:8. The server pushes an `inbox.changed` event over the SSE stream the open app is subscribed to (foreground); the phone refreshes its inbox, decrypts the message, fetches your bundle (or applies your template manifest), and shows the native row within ~1s. If the app is backgrounded, FCM wakes it and the inbox refresh happens on the next foreground.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:471:- **`410 plugin missing, revoked, or not owned by sender`** — `plugin_id` (the row UUID) is wrong, or you accidentally used `plugin_identifier`. The two are distinct (see §5 vs §6).
.\docs\integration-guide.md:472:- **`410 recipient has no active devices`** — the user has no enrolled device (signed up but never opened the app, or revoked all devices). FCM availability is *not* required; messages are stored regardless and pulled via `/v1/messages/inbox`.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:475:- **`410 plugin missing, revoked, not live-type, or not owned by sender`** (cards upsert) — the plugin row's `card_type` isn't `"live"`, or the row has a non-null `revoked_at`, or the publish row's `sender_id` doesn't match the signed envelope's sender. The error message is intentionally generic so a probing caller can't distinguish the cases (don't leak which plugin UUIDs exist).
.\docs\integration-guide.md:476:- **`410 no active pairing`** (cards upsert) — the recipient user has not paired with your sender, or the pairing has been revoked. The user needs to re-scan your pairing QR.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:482:- **`HostPreviewValidationError: hostPreview.X is N UTF-8 bytes; max is M`** — caught at `client.send_to` time. Trim the offending field; see §2 for the caps. UTF-8 byte counts, not characters — emoji and accented characters cost more than one byte.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:483:- **Row shows "New message from {sender}" with fallback text only** — your message was sent without a `hostPreview` block, or the block was malformed (logged + ignored on the device). The detail view still loads the plugin and renders normally; only the row is generic. Add a valid `hostPreview` and re-send.

.\docs\integration-guide.md:11:- **Script** (`renderer: "script"`) — a JavaScript bundle running inside a sandboxed WebView. Maximum flexibility; you ship a `render(payload)` function that returns HTML. Buttons POST through `platform.network.fetch`.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:12:- **Template** (`renderer: "template"`) — no JavaScript. You ship a small JSON manifest that maps fields out of your payload via JSONPath (`$.title`, `$.body.summary`) into a native Material 3 card. Buttons are host-rendered and the host POSTs the decrypted payload to the action's declared endpoint. Faster, lighter, no JS attack surface; constrained to a fixed set of layouts.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:16:- **Event** (`card_type: "event"`) — the default. Each `send_to` produces a new immutable inbox row. Good for notifications, alerts, transactional events.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:17:- **Live** (`card_type: "live"`) — persistent, upsertable. Subsequent upserts to the same `card_key` replace the previous payload (highest `sequence_number` wins). Good for status cards that change over time (delivery progress, market position, sensor reading). Server-enforced 48h TTL; you re-upsert to extend.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:19:In every case you also need **backend code** that publishes the plugin once and sends payloads on demand, plus (for script renderer) an HTTP endpoint that receives the action callback.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:21:The Syncler inbox shows a *native* row for every message — sender name, title, subtitle, summary, arrival time — pulled from the `hostPreview` block you embed in your payload (§2). The detail view that opens on tap is what your script bundle's `render()` or your template manifest produces.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:27:- **Native row rendering** from your `hostPreview` block (title / subtitle / summary) plus the server's arrival time (HH:mm for today, MMM d for older).
.\docs\integration-guide.md:30:- **Inbox search** (case-insensitive substring) over title, subtitle, summary, sender name, AND any tokens you supplied in `hostPreview.searchText`.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:34:- **Revocation UX** — if you revoke a plugin version with a `compromised` reason, the host refuses to execute the bundle on the device and shows a security banner instead. See §5.5.

.\docs\integration-guide.md:36:- **Cross-device dismiss.** When the user dismisses a message on device A, the server marks `DeliveryStatus.dismissed_at` for that device. .\docs\integration-guide.md:423:`https://your-app.example.com/api/action` accepts whatever body the host POSTs when the user taps an action button. The shape depends on which renderer you chose:
.\docs\integration-guide.md:425:**Script renderer** — your `onclick` handler builds the body via `platform.network.fetch`. In the §3 example that's:
.\docs\integration-guide.md:434:**Template renderer** — the host POSTs the **full decrypted payload** as the body, verbatim. There's no JS hook to intervene. Your endpoint receives the whole payload JSON; pull whatever fields you need server-side. No `Authorization` header is added by the host (the user's Syncler bearer token never reaches your endpoint — security boundary). If you need request authentication, HMAC the payload using a sender-specific secret your backend shares out of band with itself, or rely on TLS + endpoint allowlisting alone.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:436:Note: the platform does **not** inject `device_id` into the body for you in V1. If you need to distinguish which device acted, include a sender-generated identifier in your payload and (for script renderer) have the plugin echo it back. For template renderer, your `card_key` (or any other field in the payload) serves the same dedupe role. Dedupe by `item_id` / `card_key` alone if a single tap is what you care about.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:464:8. The server pushes an `inbox.changed` event over the SSE stream the open app is subscribed to (foreground); the phone refreshes its inbox, decrypts the message, fetches your bundle (or applies your template manifest), and shows the native row within ~1s. If the app is backgrounded, FCM wakes it and the inbox refresh happens on the next foreground.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:471:- **`410 plugin missing, revoked, or not owned by sender`** — `plugin_id` (the row UUID) is wrong, or you accidentally used `plugin_identifier`. The two are distinct (see §5 vs §6).
.\docs\integration-guide.md:472:- **`410 recipient has no active devices`** — the user has no enrolled device (signed up but never opened the app, or revoked all devices). FCM availability is *not* required; messages are stored regardless and pulled via `/v1/messages/inbox`.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:475:- **`410 plugin missing, revoked, not live-type, or not owned by sender`** (cards upsert) — the plugin row's `card_type` isn't `"live"`, or the row has a non-null `revoked_at`, or the publish row's `sender_id` doesn't match the signed envelope's sender. The error message is intentionally generic so a probing caller can't distinguish the cases (don't leak which plugin UUIDs exist).
.\docs\integration-guide.md:476:- **`410 no active pairing`** (cards upsert) — the recipient user has not paired with your sender, or the pairing has been revoked. The user needs to re-scan your pairing QR.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:482:- **`HostPreviewValidationError: hostPreview.X is N UTF-8 bytes; max is M`** — caught at `client.send_to` time. Trim the offending field; see §2 for the caps. UTF-8 byte counts, not characters — emoji and accented characters cost more than one byte.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:483:- **Row shows "New message from {sender}" with fallback text only** — your message was sent without a `hostPreview` block, or the block was malformed (logged + ignored on the device). The detail view still loads the plugin and renders normally; only the row is generic. Add a valid `hostPreview` and re-send.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:503:1. **Revoke the device**: Go to **Settings -> Devices** on a trusted device and revoke the lost one. This immediately kills its network access and SSE stream.

  13: 
  14: from cryptography.hazmat.primitives import serialization

  16:     Ed25519PrivateKey,
  17:     Ed25519PublicKey,
  18: )
  19: from cryptography.hazmat.primitives.ciphers.aead import AESGCM
  20:

  22: 
  23: 
  24: def b64(value: bytes) -> str:
  25:     return base64.b64encode(value).decode("ascii")
  26: 
  27: 
  28: def b64d(value: str) -> bytes:
  29:     return base64.b64decode(value)
  30: 
  31: 
  32: def random_nonce() -> bytes:
  33:     return secrets.token_bytes(AES_GCM_NONCE_BYTES)
  34: 
  35: 
  36: def canonical_json(fields: dict[str, Any]) -> bytes:
  37:     return json.dumps(fields, sort_keys=True, separators=(",", ":")).encode("utf-8")

  80: 
  81: 
  82: def load_private_key(path: str) -> Ed25519PrivateKey:
  83:     """Load an Ed25519 private key from a PEM file. Generate one if absent."""
  84:     expanded = os.path.expanduser(path)
  85:     if not os.path.exists(expanded):
  86:         return generate_and_save_private_key(expanded)
  87:     with open(expanded, "rb") as f:
  88:         data = f.read()
  89:     return serialization.load_pem_private_key(data, password=None)
  90: 
  91: 
  92: def generate_and_save_private_key(path: str) -> Ed25519PrivateKey:
  93:     key = Ed25519PrivateKey.generate()
  94:     pem = key.private_bytes(
  95:         encoding=serialization.Encoding.PEM,
  96:         format=serialization.PrivateFormat.PKCS8,
  97:         encryption_algorithm=serialization.NoEncryption(),
  98:     )
  99:     os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(path) or ".", exist_ok=True)
 100:     with open(path, "wb") as f:
 101:         f.write(pem)
 102:     os.chmod(path, 0o600)
 103:     return key
 104: 
 105: 
 106: def public_key_raw(key: Ed25519PrivateKey) -> bytes:
 107:     return key.public_key().public_bytes(
 108:         encoding=serialization.Encoding.Raw,
 109:         format=serialization.PublicFormat.Raw,
 110:     )
 111: 
 112: 
 113: def encrypt_payload(
 114:     *,
 115:     pairing_key: bytes,
 116:     plaintext: bytes,
 117:     aad: bytes,
 118: ) -> tuple[bytes, bytes]:
 119:     """Returns (nonce, ciphertext_with_tag)."""
 120:     if len(pairing_key) != 32:
 121:         raise ValueError("pairing_key must be 32 bytes")
 122:     nonce = random_nonce()
 123:     ciphertext = AESGCM(pairing_key).encrypt(nonce, plaintext, aad)
 124:     return nonce, ciphertext

   1: """HostPreview ג€” structured metadata the host renders natively as an inbox row.
   2: 
   3: The host reads this block from the decrypted payload before invoking the
   4: plugin's ``render(payload)``. The plugin still receives the full payload for
   5: the detail view; ``hostPreview`` is purely additive.
   6: 
   7: Wire contract:
   8: - Required: ``title`` (<= 80 UTF-8 bytes).
   9: - Optional: ``subtitle`` (<= 120), ``summary`` (<= 240),
  10:   ``searchText`` (list of <= 16 entries, each <= 64 UTF-8 bytes).
  11: - Serialized ``hostPreview`` must be <= 2048 UTF-8 bytes.
  12: 
  13: Missing or invalid ``hostPreview`` ג†’ the host renders a generic
  14: "New message from {sender_name}" row.
  15: """
  16: 
  17: from __future__ import annotations
  18: 
  19: import json
  20: from typing import Any, NotRequired, TypedDict
  21: 
  22: 
  23: class HostPreview(TypedDict):
  24:     title: str
  25:     subtitle: NotRequired[str]
  26:     summary: NotRequired[str]
  27:     searchText: NotRequired[list[str]]
  28: 
  29: 
  30: HOST_PREVIEW_KEY = "hostPreview"
  31: 
  32: TITLE_MAX_BYTES = 80
  33: SUBTITLE_MAX_BYTES = 120
  34: SUMMARY_MAX_BYTES = 240
  35: SEARCH_TEXT_MAX_ENTRIES = 16
  36: SEARCH_TEXT_ENTRY_MAX_BYTES = 64
  37: TOTAL_MAX_BYTES = 2048
  38: 
  39: 
  40: class HostPreviewValidationError(ValueError):
  41:     """Raised when a payload's hostPreview block violates the contract."""
  42: 
  43: 
  44: def validate_host_preview(value: Any) -> None:
  45:     """Validate a hostPreview block in-place. Raises HostPreviewValidationError
  46:     with a single explanatory message describing the first failure.
  47: 
  48:     No-op if ``value`` is None or not a dict (the host will fall back to the
  49:     generic row). Senders who want explicit feedback should call this from
  50:     their send path.
  51:     """
  52:     if value is None:
  53:         return
  54:     if not isinstance(value, dict):
  55:         raise HostPreviewValidationError("hostPreview must be a JSON object")
  56: 
  57:     title = value.get("title")
  58:     if not isinstance(title, str) or not title.strip():
  59:         raise HostPreviewValidationError("hostPreview.title is required and must be a non-empty string")
  60:     _check_bytes("title", title, TITLE_MAX_BYTES)
  61: 
  62:     if "subtitle" in value:
  63:         if not isinstance(value["subtitle"], str):
  64:             raise HostPreviewValidationError("hostPreview.subtitle must be a string")
  65:         _check_bytes("subtitle", value["subtitle"], SUBTITLE_MAX_BYTES)
  66: 
  67:     if "summary" in value:
  68:         if not isinstance(value["summary"], str):
  69:             raise HostPreviewValidationError("hostPreview.summary must be a string")
  70:         _check_bytes("summary", value["summary"], SUMMARY_MAX_BYTES)
  71: 
  72:     if "searchText" in value:
  73:         tokens = value["searchText"]
  74:         if not isinstance(tokens, list):
  75:             raise HostPreviewValidationError("hostPreview.searchText must be a list of strings")
  76:         if len(tokens) > SEARCH_TEXT_MAX_ENTRIES:
  77:             raise HostPreviewValidationError(
  78:                 f"hostPreview.searchText has {len(tokens)} entries; max is {SEARCH_TEXT_MAX_ENTRIES}"
  79:             )
  80:         for i, token in enumerate(tokens):
  81:             if not isinstance(token, str):
  82:                 raise HostPreviewValidationError(
  83:                     f"hostPreview.searchText[{i}] must be a string"
  84:                 )
  85:             _check_bytes(f"searchText[{i}]", token, SEARCH_TEXT_ENTRY_MAX_BYTES)
  86: 
  87:     # Total serialized size cap. Senders who want a richer preview should
  88:     # trim summary or searchText rather than dropping fields. `ensure_ascii=False`
  89:     # keeps the byte count byte-identical to sdk-plugin's TextEncoder(JSON.stringify(...)),
  90:     # which encodes non-ASCII characters raw (the JS default).
  91:     serialized = json.dumps(value, separators=(",", ":"), ensure_ascii=False).encode("utf-8")
  92:     if len(serialized) > TOTAL_MAX_BYTES:
  93:         raise HostPreviewValidationError(
  94:             f"hostPreview serialized size {len(serialized)} bytes exceeds {TOTAL_MAX_BYTES} byte cap"
  95:         )
  96: 
  97: 
  98: def _check_bytes(field_name: str, text: str, max_bytes: int) -> None:
  99:     size = len(text.encode("utf-8"))
 100:     if size > max_bytes:
 101:         raise HostPreviewValidationError(
 102:             f"hostPreview.{field_name} is {size} UTF-8 bytes; max is {max_bytes}"
 103:         )

 275:             "expires_at": expires_at,
 276:         }
 277: 
 278:         resp = self.session.post(f"{self.base_url}/v1/messages/send", json=body, timeout=10)
 279:         if resp.status_code == 401:
 280:             raise SignatureError("server rejected envelope signature")
 281:         if resp.status_code == 410:
 282:             detail = resp.json().get("detail", "")
 283:             if "plugin" in detail:
 284:                 raise PluginRevokedError(detail)
 285:             raise RecipientUnreachableError(detail or "recipient unreachable")
 286:         if resp.status_code == 409:
 287:             raise SynclerError("nonce replay or pairing conflict")
 288:         resp.raise_for_status()
 289:         data = resp.json()
 290:         return SendResult(message_id=data["message_id"], expires_at=data["expires_at"])
 291: 
 292:     # ---------------------------- Plugin publishing ------------------------
 293: 
 294:     def publish_plugin(
 295:         self,
 296:         *,
 297:         plugin_identifier: str,
 298:         version: str,
 299:         manifest_hash: bytes,
 300:         bundle_hash: bytes,
 301:         bundle_signature: bytes,
 302:         signed_bundle_url: str,
 303:         capabilities: list[str],
 304:         endpoints: list[str],
 305:         renderer: str = "script",
 306:         template: dict[str, Any] | None = None,
 307:         card_type: str = "event",
 308:         card_key_path: str | None = None,
 309:     ) -> dict[str, Any]:
 310:         """Publish a new plugin version. Returns the server response (with
 311:         ``plugin_row_id`` which the sender then uses in messages).
 312: 
 313:         Phase 3a: pass ``renderer="template"`` plus a ``template`` block to
 314:         ship a native Compose-rendered card instead of a WebView bundle.
 315: 
 316:         Phase 3b: pass ``card_type="live"`` plus a ``card_key_path`` (JSONPath
 317:         yielding the stable key for the card) to enable persistent,
 318:         upsertable live cards.
 319:         """
 320:         self._require_sender_id()
 321:         body: dict[str, Any] = {
 322:             "sender_id": self._canonical_sender_id(),
 323:             "plugin_identifier": plugin_identifier,
 324:             "version": version,
 325:             "manifest_hash": b64(manifest_hash),
 326:             "bundle_hash": b64(bundle_hash),
 327:             "signature": b64(bundle_signature),
 328:             "signed_bundle_url": signed_bundle_url,
 329:             "capabilities": capabilities,
 330:             "endpoints": endpoints,
 331:         }
 332:         # Mirror the server's `_publish_envelope` conditional inclusion.
 333:         if renderer != "script":
 334:             body["renderer"] = renderer
 335:         if template is not None:
 336:             body["template"] = template
 337:         if card_type != "event":
 338:             body["card_type"] = card_type
 339:         if card_key_path is not None:
 340:             body["card_key_path"] = card_key_path
 341: 
 342:         body["sender_signature"] = b64(self.private_key.sign(canonical_json(body)))
 343:         resp = self.session.post(f"{self.base_url}/v1/plugins/publish", json=body, timeout=10)
 344:         resp.raise_for_status()
 345:         return resp.json()
 346: 
 347:     def upsert_card(
 348:         self,
 349:         *,
 350:         user_id: str,
 351:         plugin_id: str,
 352:         card_key: str,
 353:         encrypted_payload: bytes,
 354:         nonce: bytes,
 355:         sequence_number: int,
 356:         expires_at: datetime,
 357:     ) -> dict[str, Any]:
 358:         """Upsert a persistent live card for a user. Fires card.upsert SSE.
 359: 
 360:         UUIDs are normalized via [_canon_uuid] before signing so an uppercase
 361:         or braced caller input produces the same canonical bytes as the
 362:         server-side `str(uuid.UUID(...))` form. Without this, a sender-side
 363:         self-401 can sneak in on UUIDs that look fine to the eye but
 364:         differ in case (Codex consultation 63 YELLOW follow-up).
 365:         """
 366:         self._require_sender_id()
 367:         body: dict[str, Any] = {
 368:             "sender_id": self._canonical_sender_id(),
 369:             "user_id": _canon_uuid(user_id),
 370:             "plugin_id": _canon_uuid(plugin_id),
 371:             "card_key": card_key,
 372:             "encrypted_payload": b64(encrypted_payload),
 373:             "nonce": b64(nonce),
 374:             "sequence_number": sequence_number,
 375:             "expires_at": expires_at.isoformat().replace("+00:00", "Z"),
 376:         }
 377: 
 378:         # Envelope for upsert includes card_type: live. `sequence_number`
 379:         # stays as int here to match the server's canonical envelope
 380:         # (see routers/cards.py:_build_upsert_envelope_bytes).
 381:         envelope = dict(body)
 382:         envelope["card_type"] = "live"
 383:         body["envelope_signature"] = b64(self.private_key.sign(canonical_json(envelope)))
 384: 
 385:         resp = self.session.post(f"{self.base_url}/v1/cards/upsert", json=body, timeout=10)
 386:         resp.raise_for_status()
 387:         return resp.json()
 388: 
 389:     def delete_card(
 390:         self,
 391:         *,
 392:         user_id: str,
 393:         card_key: str,
 394:     ) -> None:
 395:         """Delete a persistent live card for a specific user. Fires card.delete SSE.
 396: 
 397:         Phase 3b: `user_id` is REQUIRED in the canonical signed envelope so a
 398:         delete signature for one user's card cannot be replayed against
 399:         another user's card with the same (sender, card_key). Mirrors the
 400:         server's `_build_delete_envelope_bytes`. Closes Codex consultation
 401:         62 RED #5.
 402:         """
 403:         self._require_sender_id()
 404:         sender_id = self._canonical_sender_id()
 405:         user_id_canonical = _canon_uuid(user_id)
 406:         envelope = canonical_json(
 407:             {
 408:                 "sender_id": sender_id,
 409:                 "user_id": user_id_canonical,
 410:                 "card_key": card_key,
 411:             }
 412:         )
 413:         body = {
 414:             "sender_id": sender_id,
 415:             "user_id": user_id_canonical,
 416:             "card_key": card_key,
 417:             "envelope_signature": b64(self.private_key.sign(envelope)),
 418:         }
 419:         resp = self.session.post(f"{self.base_url}/v1/cards/delete", json=body, timeout=10)
 420:         resp.raise_for_status()
 421: 
 422:     # Accepted classifications for the optional ``reason`` field on revoke.
 423:     # The host renders different UX per reason: silent for ``superseded``,
 424:     # security alert with refuse-to-execute for ``compromised``, neutral
 425:     # "no longer available" banner for ``sender_disabled``. ``unspecified``
 426:     # is the conservative default for legacy revokes with no reason given;
 427:     # callers SHOULD always supply a real classification.
 428:     REVOCATION_REASONS = ("superseded", "compromised", "sender_disabled", "unspecified")
 429: 
 430:     def revoke_plugin(
 431:         self,
 432:         *,
 433:         plugin_row_id: str,
 434:         reason: str | None = None,
 435:     ) -> None:
 436:         """Revoke a previously-published plugin row, optionally with a
 437:         classified reason.
 438: 
 439:         ``reason`` must be one of :attr:`REVOCATION_REASONS` or None. If
 440:         supplied, the value is included in the canonical signed envelope so
 441:         an in-flight MITM cannot strip a security classification down to a
 442:         harmless one. The server's revoke service is monotone: a higher-
 443:         severity reason can overwrite a lower one (``superseded`` ->
 444:         ``compromised``), but downgrades are silently ignored.
 445: 
 446:         Returns None on success; raises for HTTP errors.
 447:         """
 448:         self._require_sender_id()
 449:         if reason is not None and reason not in self.REVOCATION_REASONS:
 450:             raise SynclerError(
 451:                 f"reason must be one of {self.REVOCATION_REASONS}; got {reason!r}"
 452:             )
 453:         envelope: dict[str, str] = {
 454:             "sender_id": self._canonical_sender_id(),
 455:             "plugin_row_id": _canon_uuid(plugin_row_id),
 456:         }
 457:         if reason is not None:
 458:             envelope["reason"] = reason
 459:         signature = self.private_key.sign(canonical_json(envelope))
 460:         body: dict[str, Any] = dict(envelope)
 461:         body["sender_signature"] = b64(signature)
 462:         resp = self.session.post(
 463:             f"{self.base_url}/v1/plugins/revoke", json=body, timeout=10
 464:         )
 465:         resp.raise_for_status()
 466:

 470:         if self.sender_id is None:

   3: from __future__ import annotations
   4: 
   5: import uuid
   6: from datetime import UTC, datetime, timedelta
   7: 
   8: from sqlalchemy import and_, select
   9: from sqlalchemy.ext.asyncio import AsyncSession
  10: 
  11: from app.models import LiveCard, Pairing, Plugin
  12: 
  13: # Server-enforced 48h TTL ceiling. Sender-supplied `expires_at` is clamped
  14: # against `now + MAX_TTL` so a malicious or buggy sender can't squat a card
  15: # slot indefinitely (Codex consultation 62 RED #4). Aligns with the Phase 3b
  16: # plan in .triad/50-agreement-and-plan.md.
  17: MAX_TTL = timedelta(hours=48)
  18: 
  19: 
  20: class CardError(Exception):
  21:     """Base class for card service errors."""
  22: 
  23: 
  24: class CardNotFoundError(CardError):
  25:     """Card not found."""
  26: 
  27: 
  28: class PluginInactiveError(CardError):
  29:     """Plugin missing, revoked, or not owned by sender."""
  30: 
  31: 
  32: class PairingMissingError(CardError):
  33:     """No active (sender_id, user_id) pairing."""
  34: 
  35: 
  36: class ExpiredEnvelopeError(CardError):
  37:     """expires_at is not in the future or exceeds the server-enforced cap."""
  38: 
  39: 
  40: class SequenceNumberRegressionError(CardError):
  41:     """New sequence number is not greater than existing."""
  42: 
  43: 
  44: async def upsert_live_card(
  45:     db: AsyncSession,
  46:     *,
  47:     sender_id: uuid.UUID,
  48:     user_id: uuid.UUID,
  49:     plugin_id: uuid.UUID,
  50:     card_key: str,
  51:     encrypted_payload: bytes,
  52:     nonce: bytes,
  53:     sequence_number: int,
  54:     expires_at: datetime,
  55: ) -> LiveCard:
  56:     now = datetime.now(UTC)
  57:     # TTL enforcement (Codex consultation 62 RED #4): reject already-expired
  58:     # expires_at and clamp anything beyond the 48h cap. Mirrors the
  59:     # `store_message` MAX_RETENTION pattern in services/messages.py.
  60:     if expires_at <= now:
  61:         raise ExpiredEnvelopeError("expires_at is not in the future")
  62:     if expires_at > now + MAX_TTL:
  63:         raise ExpiredEnvelopeError(
  64:             f"expires_at exceeds the {int(MAX_TTL.total_seconds() // 3600)}h live-card cap"
  65:         )
  66: 
  67:     # Pairing check (Codex consultation 62 RED #3): live-card upsert MUST
  68:     # require an active (sender_id, user_id) pairing, same as the message
  69:     # store path. Without this, any registered sender could push live cards
  70:     # to any user they happen to know the UUID of.
  71:     pairing_result = await db.execute(
  72:         select(Pairing).where(
  73:             and_(
  74:                 Pairing.sender_id == sender_id,
  75:                 Pairing.user_id == user_id,
  76:                 Pairing.revoked_at.is_(None),
  77:             ),
  78:         ),
  79:     )
  80:     if pairing_result.scalar_one_or_none() is None:
  81:         raise PairingMissingError("no active pairing")
  82: 
  83:     # Plugin lookup (Codex consultation 62 RED #2): include the
  84:     # `Plugin.revoked_at.is_(None)` filter so revoked plugins cannot upsert
  85:     # live cards (matches the messages service `_plugin` pattern).
  86:     result = await db.execute(
  87:         select(Plugin).where(
  88:             and_(
  89:                 Plugin.id == plugin_id,
  90:                 Plugin.sender_id == sender_id,
  91:                 Plugin.card_type == "live",
  92:                 Plugin.revoked_at.is_(None),
  93:             )
  94:         )
  95:     )
  96:     plugin = result.scalar_one_or_none()
  97:     if plugin is None:
  98:         raise PluginInactiveError(
  99:             "plugin missing, revoked, not live-type, or not owned by sender"
 100:         )
 101: 
 102:     # 2. Upsert with sequence number check.
 103:     existing_result = await db.execute(
 104:         select(LiveCard).where(
 105:             and_(
 106:                 LiveCard.sender_id == sender_id,
 107:                 LiveCard.user_id == user_id,
 108:                 LiveCard.card_key == card_key,
 109:             )
 110:         )
 111:     )
 112:     existing = existing_result.scalar_one_or_none()
 113:     
 114:     now = datetime.now(UTC)
 115:     if existing:
 116:         if sequence_number <= existing.sequence_number:
 117:             raise SequenceNumberRegressionError(
 118:                 f"sequence_number {sequence_number} not greater than {existing.sequence_number}"
 119:             )
 120:         
 121:         existing.encrypted_payload = encrypted_payload
 122:         existing.nonce = nonce
 123:         existing.sequence_number = sequence_number
 124:         existing.updated_at = now
 125:         existing.expires_at = expires_at
 126:         card = existing
 127:     else:
 128:         card = LiveCard(
 129:             id=uuid.uuid4(),
 130:             user_id=user_id,
 131:             sender_id=sender_id,
 132:             plugin_id=plugin_id,
 133:             card_key=card_key,
 134:             encrypted_payload=encrypted_payload,
 135:             nonce=nonce,
 136:             sequence_number=sequence_number,
 137:             created_at=now,
 138:             updated_at=now,
 139:             expires_at=expires_at,
 140:         )
 141:         db.add(card)
 142: 
 143:     await db.commit()
 144:     await db.refresh(card)
 145:     return card
 146:

 149:     db: AsyncSession,

 151:     sender_id: uuid.UUID,

 153:     card_key: str,

 170: async def get_live_cards_for_user(
 171:     db: AsyncSession,
 172:     *,
 173:     user_id: uuid.UUID,
 174: ) -> list[LiveCard]:
 175:     now = datetime.now(UTC)
 176:     result = await db.execute(
 177:         select(LiveCard).where(
 178:             and_(
 179:                 LiveCard.user_id == user_id,
 180:                 LiveCard.expires_at > now,
 181:             )
 182:         )
 183:     )
 184:     return list(result.scalars().all())
 185: 
 186: 
 187: async def prune_expired_cards(db: AsyncSession) -> int:
 188:     """Delete cards past their expires_at."""
 189:     now = datetime.now(UTC)
 190:     expired = await db.execute(select(LiveCard).where(LiveCard.expires_at <= now))
 191:     count = 0
 192:     for card in expired.scalars().all():
 193:         await db.delete(card)
 194:         count += 1
 195:     if count > 0:
 196:         await db.commit()
 197:     return count

  44: def _b64(value: bytes) -> str:
  45:     return base64.b64encode(value).decode("ascii")
  46: 
  47: 
  48: def _publish_envelope(payload: PluginPublishRequest) -> bytes:
  49:     envelope: dict[str, object] = {
  50:         "sender_id": str(payload.sender_id),
  51:         "plugin_identifier": payload.plugin_identifier,
  52:         "version": payload.version,
  53:         "manifest_hash": payload.manifest_hash,
  54:         "bundle_hash": payload.bundle_hash,
  55:         "signature": payload.signature,
  56:         "signed_bundle_url": payload.signed_bundle_url,
  57:         "capabilities": payload.capabilities,
  58:         "endpoints": payload.endpoints,
  59:     }
  60:     # Phase 3a: renderer/template are conditionally included so a pre-Phase-3a
  61:     # sender (which doesn't know about these fields and signs an envelope
  62:     # without them) still verifies. Senders shipping a template must include
  63:     # both in their canonical signing envelope; senders defaulting to script
  64:     # must omit them. The sender-side SDK (`sdk-python/syncler/client.py`)
  65:     # mirrors this rule.
  66:     if payload.renderer != "script":
  67:         envelope["renderer"] = payload.renderer
  68:     if payload.template is not None:
  69:         envelope["template"] = payload.template.model_dump(mode="json")
  70:     # Phase 3b: card_type/card_key_path are conditionally included.
  71:     if payload.card_type != "event":
  72:         envelope["card_type"] = payload.card_type
  73:     if payload.card_key_path is not None:
  74:         envelope["card_key_path"] = payload.card_key_path
  75:     return json.dumps(envelope, sort_keys=True, separators=(",", ":")).encode("utf-8")
  76: 
  77: 
  78: def _revoke_envelope(payload: PluginRevokeRequest) -> bytes:
  79:     # Canonical 3-field envelope. Reason is part of the signed bytes so a
  80:     # man-in-the-middle can't strip a "compromised" reason down to a silent
  81:     # "superseded". Backwards compat with M8.1 clients: when reason is None
  82:     # we omit it from the envelope so the signature shape matches.
  83:     envelope: dict[str, str] = {
  84:         "sender_id": str(payload.sender_id),
  85:         "plugin_row_id": str(payload.plugin_row_id),
  86:     }
  87:     if payload.reason is not None:
  88:         envelope["reason"] = payload.reason
  89:     return json.dumps(envelope, sort_keys=True, separators=(",", ":")).encode("utf-8")
  90: 
  91: 
  92: @router.post("/publish", response_model=PluginPublishResponse, status_code=status.HTTP_201_CREATED)
  93: async def publish(
  94:     payload: PluginPublishRequest,
  95:     request: Request,
  96:     # Pre-auth IP bucket ג€” cheap, prevents body-parsing DoS from anonymous
  97:     # callers. The per-sender bucket is applied below, after sig verification.
  98:     _: None = Depends(rate_limit("message_send_ip")),
  99:     db: AsyncSession = Depends(get_db),
 100: ) -> PluginPublishResponse:
 101:     try:
 102:         sender = await get_active_sender(db, payload.sender_id)
 103:     except SenderNotFoundError as exc:
 104:         raise HTTPException(status_code=404, detail="sender not found") from exc
 105:     except SenderRevokedError as exc:
 106:         raise HTTPException(status_code=410, detail="sender revoked") from exc
 107: 
 108:     sender_sig = decode_base64(payload.sender_signature, field_name="sender_signature", exact=64)
 109:     if not verify_message_envelope(sender.public_key, _publish_envelope(payload), sender_sig):
 110:         raise HTTPException(status_code=401, detail="invalid sender signature")
 111: 
 112:     # Per-sender bucket AFTER signature verification ג€” a spoofer cannot inflate
 113:     # someone else's bucket by setting a foreign sender_id in the body, because
 114:     # they cannot forge the matching Ed25519 signature.
 115:     request.state.sender_id = str(payload.sender_id)
 116:     await check_rate_limit(db, request, RATE_LIMITS["plugin_publish"])
 117: 
 118:     try:
 119:         plugin = await publish_plugin(
 120:             db,
 121:             sender_id=sender.id,
 122:             plugin_identifier=payload.plugin_identifier,
 123:             version=payload.version,
 124:             manifest_hash=decode_base64(payload.manifest_hash, field_name="manifest_hash", exact=32),
 125:             bundle_hash=decode_base64(payload.bundle_hash, field_name="bundle_hash", exact=32),
 126:             signature=decode_base64(payload.signature, field_name="signature", exact=64),
 127:             signed_bundle_url=payload.signed_bundle_url,
 128:             capabilities=payload.capabilities,
 129:             endpoints=payload.endpoints,
 130:             renderer=payload.renderer,
 131:             template=(payload.template.model_dump(mode="json") if payload.template else None),
 132:             card_type=payload.card_type,
 133:             card_key_path=payload.card_key_path,
 134:         )
 135:     except InvalidVersionError as exc:
 136:         raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail=str(exc)) from exc
 137:     except VersionRegressionError as exc:
 138:         raise HTTPException(status_code=409, detail=str(exc)) from exc
 139:     except DuplicateVersionError as exc:
 140:         raise HTTPException(status_code=409, detail=str(exc)) from exc
 141: 
 142:     return PluginPublishResponse(
 143:         plugin_row_id=plugin.id,
 144:         plugin_identifier=plugin.plugin_identifier,
 145:         version=plugin.version,
 146:         created_at=plugin.created_at,
 147:     )
 148: 
 149: 
 150: @router.get("/{sender_id}/{plugin_identifier}/latest", response_model=PluginLatestResponse)
 151: async def latest(
 152:     sender_id: uuid.UUID,
 153:     plugin_identifier: str,
 154:     _: None = Depends(rate_limit("manifest_fetch")),
 155:     db: AsyncSession = Depends(get_db),
 156: ) -> PluginLatestResponse:
 157:     try:
 158:         plugin = await get_latest_for_plugin(
 159:             db, sender_id=sender_id, plugin_identifier=plugin_identifier
 160:         )
 161:     except PluginNotFoundError as exc:
 162:         raise HTTPException(status_code=404, detail="plugin not found") from exc
 163: 
 164:     return PluginLatestResponse(
 165:         plugin_row_id=plugin.id,
 166:         sender_id=plugin.sender_id,

 186: @router.get("/by-id/{plugin_row_id}", response_model=PluginLatestResponse)
 187: async def by_id(
 188:     plugin_row_id: uuid.UUID,
 189:     # IP-based bucket: /by-id is unauthenticated and has no sender_id in
 190:     # the path for the per-sender bucket to key off. message_send_ip is
 191:     # the cheap pre-auth bucket we use for the same shape elsewhere.
 192:     _: None = Depends(rate_limit("message_send_ip")),
 193:     db: AsyncSession = Depends(get_db),
 194: ) -> PluginLatestResponse:
 195:     """Resolve a plugin manifest by its exact row UUID.
 196: 
 197:     Devices use this for historical lookups (an inbox message carries the
 198:     plugin_row_id it was originally validated against; resolving by row
 199:     UUID guarantees the device renders against the EXACT bundle that was
 200:     in effect at message-send time, even after the sender publishes a
 201:     newer or revoked version under the same plugin_identifier).
 202: 
 203:     Unlike `/latest`, this endpoint returns revoked rows too ג€” with
 204:     `revoked_at` and `revocation_reason` populated so the device can
 205:     apply differentiated UX (refuse-to-execute for `compromised`,
 206:     neutral fallback for `sender_disabled`, etc.).
 207:     """
 208:     try:
 209:         plugin = await get_plugin_by_id(db, plugin_row_id=plugin_row_id)
 210:     except PluginNotFoundError as exc:
 211:         raise HTTPException(status_code=404, detail="plugin not found") from exc
 212: 
 213:     return PluginLatestResponse(
 214:         plugin_row_id=plugin.id,
 215:         sender_id=plugin.sender_id,
 216:         plugin_identifier=plugin.plugin_identifier,
 217:         version=plugin.version,
 218:         signed_bundle_url=plugin.signed_bundle_url,
 219:         manifest_hash=_b64(plugin.manifest_hash),
 220:         bundle_hash=_b64(plugin.bundle_hash),
 221:         signature=_b64(plugin.signature),
 222:         capabilities=plugin.capabilities,
 223:         endpoints=plugin.endpoints,
 224:         created_at=plugin.created_at,
 225:         revoked_at=plugin.revoked_at,
 226:         revocation_reason=plugin.revocation_reason,
 227:         renderer=plugin.renderer,
 228:         template=plugin.template,
 229:     )

 232: @router.post("/revoke", status_code=status.HTTP_204_NO_CONTENT)
 233: async def revoke(
 234:     payload: PluginRevokeRequest,
 235:     db: AsyncSession = Depends(get_db),
 236: ) -> Response:
 237:     """Sender-authenticated plugin row revoke.
 238: 
 239:     M8.1 fix: the previous public revoke endpoint allowed anyone with a
 240:     plugin UUID to wipe out a plugin. Now sender signs the revoke envelope
 241:     with their Ed25519 private key, and we also verify the row belongs to
 242:     that sender before flipping revoked_at.
 243:     """
 244:     try:
 245:         sender = await get_active_sender(db, payload.sender_id)
 246:     except SenderNotFoundError as exc:
 247:         raise HTTPException(status_code=404, detail="sender not found") from exc
 248:     except SenderRevokedError as exc:
 249:         raise HTTPException(status_code=410, detail="sender revoked") from exc
 250: 
 251:     sender_sig = decode_base64(payload.sender_signature, field_name="sender_signature", exact=64)
 252:     if not verify_message_envelope(sender.public_key, _revoke_envelope(payload), sender_sig):
 253:         raise HTTPException(status_code=401, detail="invalid sender signature")
 254: 
 255:     plugin_result = await db.execute(select(Plugin).where(Plugin.id == payload.plugin_row_id))
 256:     plugin = plugin_result.scalar_one_or_none()
 257:     if plugin is None:
 258:         raise HTTPException(status_code=404, detail="plugin not found")
 259:     if plugin.sender_id != payload.sender_id:
 260:         # Don't leak existence of foreign-sender's plugins ג€” 404 not 403.
 261:         raise HTTPException(status_code=404, detail="plugin not found")
 262: 
 263:     try:
 264:         await revoke_plugin_row(db, payload.plugin_row_id, reason=payload.reason)
 265:     except PluginNotFoundError as exc:
 266:         raise HTTPException(status_code=404, detail="plugin not found") from exc
 267:     return Response(status_code=status.HTTP_204_NO_CONTENT)

  65: def _build_envelope_bytes(payload: MessageSendRequest) -> bytes:
  66:     """Build the canonical 7-field envelope the sender signs (matches crypto-spec ײ²ֲ§4.1)."""
  67:     if payload.expires_at is None:
  68:         raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="expires_at is required")
  69:     return assemble_envelope(
  70:         {
  71:             "sender_id": str(payload.sender_id),
  72:             "user_id": str(payload.user_id),
  73:             "plugin_id": str(payload.plugin_id),
  74:             "min_plugin_version": payload.min_plugin_version or "",
  75:             "expires_at": payload.expires_at.isoformat().replace("+00:00", "Z"),

  82: @router.post("/send", response_model=MessageSendResponse, status_code=status.HTTP_201_CREATED)
  83: async def send_message(
  84:     payload: MessageSendRequest,
  85:     request: Request,
  86:     _: None = Depends(rate_limit("message_send_ip")),
  87:     db: AsyncSession = Depends(get_db),
  88: ) -> MessageSendResponse:
  89:     if payload.expires_at is None:
  90:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_400_BAD_REQUEST, detail="expires_at is required")
  91: 
  92:     try:
  93:         sender: Sender = await get_active_sender(db, payload.sender_id)
  94:     except SenderNotFoundError as exc:
  95:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_404_NOT_FOUND, detail="sender not found") from exc
  96:     except SenderRevokedError as exc:
  97:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_410_GONE, detail="sender revoked") from exc
  98: 
  99:     envelope_bytes = _build_envelope_bytes(payload)
 100:     signature = decode_base64(payload.envelope_signature, field_name="envelope_signature", exact=64)
 101: 
 102:     if not verify_message_envelope(sender.public_key, envelope_bytes, signature):
 103:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_401_UNAUTHORIZED, detail="invalid envelope signature")
 104: 
 105:     # Per-sender rate limit AFTER signature verification (so spammers can't
 106:     # inflate someone else's bucket by spoofing the body sender_id).
 107:     request.state.sender_id = str(payload.sender_id)
 108:     request.state.user_id = str(payload.user_id)
 109:     from app.middleware.rate_limit import check_rate_limit
 110:     from app.middleware.rate_limit_config import RATE_LIMITS
 111:     await check_rate_limit(db, request, RATE_LIMITS["message_send"])
 112:     await check_rate_limit(db, request, RATE_LIMITS["message_send_user_hour"])
 113: 
 114:     # Replay check AFTER signature verification (so attackers can't OOM the
 115:     # nonce registry by spamming junk). We check first to short-circuit,
 116:     # then re-mark after successful store_message so failed stores don't
 117:     # burn the nonce.
 118:     nonce_bytes = decode_base64(payload.nonce, field_name="nonce", exact=12)
 119:     registry = get_global_registry()
 120:     sender_key = str(payload.sender_id).encode("utf-8")
 121:     if registry.has(sender_key, nonce_bytes):
 122:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_409_CONFLICT, detail="nonce already used")
 123: 
 124:     try:
 125:         message = await store_message(
 126:             db,
 127:             sender_id=payload.sender_id,
 128:             user_id=payload.user_id,
 129:             plugin_id=payload.plugin_id,
 130:             encrypted_body=decode_base64(payload.encrypted_body, field_name="encrypted_body", minimum=16),
 131:             nonce=nonce_bytes,
 132:             envelope_signature=signature,
 133:             min_plugin_version=payload.min_plugin_version,
 134:             expires_at=payload.expires_at,
 135:         )
 136:     except ExpiredEnvelopeError as exc:
 137:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_400_BAD_REQUEST, detail=str(exc)) from exc
 138:     except PairingMissingError as exc:
 139:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_403_FORBIDDEN, detail="no active pairing") from exc
 140:     except PluginInactiveError as exc:
 141:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_410_GONE, detail="plugin missing, revoked, or not owned by sender") from exc
 142:     except NoActiveDeviceWithPluginError as exc:
 143:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_410_GONE, detail="recipient has no active devices") from exc
 144:     except NonceReplayError as exc:
 145:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_409_CONFLICT, detail="nonce already used") from exc
 146: 
 147:     # Mark nonce as seen ONLY after store_message succeeds; failed stores
 148:     # don't burn the nonce.
 149:     registry.mark(sender_key, nonce_bytes)
 150: 
 151:     await push_message_to_user_devices(db, message=message)
 152:     # SSE hint: nudge any device the recipient has in foreground to pull
 153:     # /v1/messages/inbox now. Devices in background rely on the FCM
 154:     # wakeup already triggered by push_message_to_user_devices.
 155:     await get_event_bus().publish_to_user(
 156:         user_id=message.user_id,
 157:         event_type="inbox.changed",
 158:         data={"message_id": str(message.id), "sent_at": message.sent_at.isoformat()},
 159:     )
 160:     return MessageSendResponse(message_id=message.id, expires_at=message.expires_at)

 213:             updated_at=c.updated_at,

  18: def decode_base64(value: str, *, field_name: str, exact: int | None = None, minimum: int | None = None) -> bytes:
  19:     try:
  20:         decoded = base64.b64decode(value, validate=True)
  21:     except (binascii.Error, ValueError) as exc:
  22:         raise ValueError(f"{field_name} must be valid base64") from exc
  23: 
  24:     if exact is not None and len(decoded) != exact:
  25:         raise ValueError(f"{field_name} must decode to {exact} bytes")
  26:     if minimum is not None and len(decoded) < minimum:
  27:         raise ValueError(f"{field_name} must decode to at least {minimum} bytes")
  28: 
  29:     return decoded

 180: class MessageInboxItem(BaseModel):
 181:     id: UUID
 182:     sender_id: UUID
 183:     plugin_id: UUID
 184:     # Stable sender-chosen identifier (e.g. "com.lottery.app"). The device
 185:     # uses this to fetch the plugin manifest at
 186:     # `/v1/plugins/{sender_id}/{plugin_identifier}/latest` and render the
 187:     # message's card via the sender's JS plugin bundle.

 195:     expires_at: datetime
 196: 
 197:     # Senders sign/encrypt with a `Z`-suffixed UTC string for `expires_at`
 198:     # (see sdk-python crypto.py + the canonicalization in
 199:     # routers/messages.py:_build_envelope_bytes). Pydantic's default datetime
 200:     # serializer emits `+00:00`, which would make the device's AAD bytes
 201:     # diverge from what the sender encrypted with and break AES-GCM decrypt.
 202:     # Force the canonical form on the wire.
 203:     @field_serializer("expires_at")

 205:         return value.isoformat().replace("+00:00", "Z")

  84: internal fun canonicalJsonBytes(fields: Map<String, Any>): ByteArray =
  85:     fields.entries.sortedBy { it.key }.joinToString(prefix = "{", postfix = "}", separator = ",") { (key, value) ->
  86:         val encodedValue = when (value) {
  87:             is Int -> value.toString()
  88:             is Long -> value.toString()
  89:             is String -> "\"${value.jsonEscape()}\""
  90:             else -> error("unsupported AAD value type: ${value::class.simpleName}")
  91:         }
  92:         "\"$key\":$encodedValue"
  93:     }.encodeToByteArray()
  94: 
  95: private fun String.jsonEscape(): String = buildString {
  96:     for (char in this@jsonEscape) {
  97:         when (char) {
  98:             '\\' -> append("\\\\")
  99:             '"' -> append("\\\"")
 100:             '\b' -> append("\\b")
 101:             '' -> append("\\f")
 102:             '\n' -> append("\\n")
 103:             '\r' -> append("\\r")
 104:             '\t' -> append("\\t")
 105:             else -> if (char.code < 0x20 || char.code > 0x7E) {
 106:                 append("\\u%04x".format(char.code))
 107:             } else {
 108:                 append(char)
 109:             }
 110:         }
 111:     }

 397: # Phase 3a ג€” template renderer.
 398: #
 399: # Layouts and per-layout required fields. Senders publish a `template` object
 400: # alongside `renderer: "template"` to declare a native Compose rendering
 401: # instead of a WebView bundle. The publish-time validator enforces the
 402: # schema constraints below so the client never has to render a malformed
 403: # template at message time (Phase 3a in `.triad/50-agreement-and-plan.md`).
 404: _TEMPLATE_LAYOUTS: frozenset[str] = frozenset({"standard_card"})
 405: _LAYOUT_REQUIRED_FIELDS: dict[str, frozenset[str]] = {
 406:     "standard_card": frozenset({"title"}),
 407: }
 408: _LAYOUT_OPTIONAL_FIELDS: dict[str, frozenset[str]] = {
 409:     "standard_card": frozenset({"subtitle", "body"}),
 410: }
 411: # Only $.dotted.path navigation is supported in V1 (no array indexing, no
 412: # wildcards, no filters). Keep the surface tight so the client-side resolver
 413: # stays small and auditable.
 414: _JSONPATH_REGEX = re.compile(r"^\$(?:\.[A-Za-z_][A-Za-z0-9_]*)+$")
 415: # Path-length cap is shared with the hostPreview value cap (200 chars).
 416: _TEMPLATE_PATH_MAX = 200
 417: _ACTION_ID_MAX = 64
 418: _ACTION_LABEL_MAX = 64
 419: _ACTION_ENDPOINT_MAX = 2048
 420: 
 421: 
 422: def _endpoint_pattern_matches(url: str, pattern: str) -> bool:
 423:     """Mirror of the Kotlin EndpointMatcher in :plugin-host. Treats `*` in
 424:     the host as `[^./]*` (no subdomain leak), `*` in the path as `[^/]*`.
 425:     Required so the client and server agree on which action endpoints are
 426:     "in" the declared-endpoints set.
 427:     """
 428:     # Find where the path starts (first `/` after the scheme).
 429:     scheme_end = pattern.find("://")
 430:     if scheme_end == -1:
 431:         path_start = len(pattern)
 432:     else:
 433:         slash_after_authority = pattern.find("/", scheme_end + 3)
 434:         path_start = slash_after_authority if slash_after_authority != -1 else len(pattern)
 435: 
 436:     out: list[str] = []
 437:     for index, character in enumerate(pattern):
 438:         if character == "*":
 439:             out.append("[^./]*" if index < path_start else "[^/]*")
 440:         else:
 441:             out.append(re.escape(character))
 442:     return re.match(f"^{''.join(out)}$", url) is not None
 443:

 445: class TemplateField(BaseModel):
 446:     """One template field ג€” a JSONPath expression that resolves against the
 447:     decrypted payload at render time."""
 448:     path: Annotated[str, Field(min_length=1, max_length=_TEMPLATE_PATH_MAX)]
 449: 
 450:     @field_validator("path")
 451:     @classmethod
 452:     def validate_path(cls, value: str) -> str:
 453:         if not _JSONPATH_REGEX.match(value):
 454:             raise ValueError(
 455:                 f"invalid JSONPath {value!r}: must match $.field(.subfield)*",
 456:             )
 457:         return value

  31: /**
  32:  * Phase 3a ג€” native Compose renderer for manifest-declared template cards.
  33:  *
  34:  * Replaces the WebView path for plugins published with `renderer == "template"`.
  35:  * The publish-time server validator (see `server/app/schemas.py`
  36:  * `TemplateObject` + `PluginPublishRequest.validate_renderer_template_pairing`)
  37:  * has already enforced:
  38:  *  - layout is in the supported set (currently only `standard_card`),
  39:  *  - JSONPath syntax is `$.field(.subfield)*`,
  40:  *  - the layout has its required fields (e.g. standard_card requires `title`),
  41:  *  - every action's `endpoint` matches one of the plugin's `endpoints` globs,
  42:  *  - action ids are unique within the template.
  43:  *
  44:  * So this renderer can trust the [TemplateBlockDto] structurally and only
  45:  * needs to defend against payload-level surprises (missing key, wrong JSON
  46:  * type at a path, oversized strings).
  47:  *
  48:  * Security: every text resolved from the payload is rendered through Compose
  49:  * [Text], which does NOT interpret markdown, HTML, or any markup ג€” so a
  50:  * malicious payload value cannot inject a clickable link or escape the card.
  51:  * Action endpoints are NOT re-validated client-side because the manifest
  52:  * was already validated server-side; if the manifest later changes (e.g. a
  53:  * sender publishes a new version), the client only sees fields the new
  54:  * manifest declares.
  55:  */
  56: @Composable
  57: fun TemplateCard(
  58:     template: TemplateBlockDto,
  59:     payloadJson: String,
  60:     @Suppress("UNUSED_PARAMETER") declaredEndpoints: List<String>,
  61:     onAction: (id: String, endpoint: String) -> Unit,
  62:     modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
  63: ) {
  64:     // Parse once and remember ג€” the same payloadJson string identity through
  65:     // the lifetime of this composable instance is the cache key.
  66:     val payload = remember(payloadJson) {
  67:         runCatching { JSONObject(payloadJson) }.getOrElse {
  68:             Timber.tag(TAG).w(it, "template card payload is not JSON")
  69:             JSONObject()
  70:         }
  71:     }
  72: 
  73:     val titlePath = template.fields["title"]?.path
  74:     val subtitlePath = template.fields["subtitle"]?.path
  75:     val bodyPath = template.fields["body"]?.path
  76: 
  77:     val title = titlePath?.let { resolveJsonPath(payload, it) }
  78:     val subtitle = subtitlePath?.let { resolveJsonPath(payload, it) }
  79:     val body = bodyPath?.let { resolveJsonPath(payload, it) }
  80: 
  81:     Column(
  82:         modifier = modifier.fillMaxSize().padding(16.dp),
  83:         verticalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(12.dp),
  84:     ) {
  85:         when (template.layout) {
  86:             "standard_card" -> StandardCard(
  87:                 title = title,
  88:                 subtitle = subtitle,
  89:                 body = body,
  90:                 actions = template.actions,
  91:                 onActionTap = { action -> onAction(action.id, action.endpoint) },
  92:             )
  93:             else -> {
  94:                 // Defense-in-depth ג€” the server validator would have rejected
  95:                 // any other layout, but if a future server-side relaxation
  96:                 // forwards an unknown layout to a stale client, surface a
  97:                 // clear diagnostic instead of crashing or rendering nothing.
  98:                 Text(
  99:                     "Unsupported template layout: ${template.layout}",
 100:                     style = MaterialTheme.typography.titleMedium,
 101:                 )
 102:             }
 103:         }
 104:     }
 105: }
