 152: /**
 153:  * Visible only for unit testing. Resolves a `$.foo.bar` JSONPath against the
 154:  * decrypted payload. Returns:
 155:  *  - the string value when the leaf is a JSON string,
 156:  *  - a JSON-encoded compact form when the leaf is a number/bool,
 157:  *  - null if any segment is missing or the leaf is an object/array/null.
 158:  *
 159:  * The publish-time validator enforces the `$.foo(.bar)*` syntax, but this
 160:  * function still tolerates a malformed input (returns null) rather than
 161:  * throwing ג€” defense against a future server change that loosens validation.
 162:  */
 163: internal fun resolveJsonPath(root: JSONObject, path: String): String? {
 164:     if (!path.startsWith("$.")) return null
 165:     val segments = path.substring(2).split('.')
 166:     if (segments.isEmpty() || segments.any { it.isEmpty() }) return null
 167: 
 168:     var current: Any? = root
 169:     for (segment in segments) {
 170:         val obj = current as? JSONObject ?: return null
 171:         if (!obj.has(segment)) return null
 172:         current = obj.opt(segment)
 173:         if (current == null || current == JSONObject.NULL) return null
 174:     }
 175:     return when (current) {
 176:         is String -> current
 177:         is Number, is Boolean -> current.toString()
 178:         else -> null
 179:     }
 180: }
 181: 
 182: /**
 183:  * Fire-and-forget POST helper used by [InboxViewModel.runTemplateAction]. The
 184:  * receiving service decides how to authenticate (HMAC over body, plugin-
 185:  * specific JWT, ג€¦); the host just attests to the user's tap.
 186:  *
 187:  * SECURITY: this builds its OWN [OkHttpClient] rather than injecting the
 188:  * `:core:network` singleton. That singleton has an `AuthTokenProvider`-backed
 189:  * interceptor (see
 190:  * [app.syncler.core.network.NetworkModule.provideAuthInterceptor]) which
 191:  * would auto-attach the user's Syncler bearer JWT to every request. Template
 192:  * action endpoints are sender-controlled (the plugin's `declaredEndpoints`
 193:  * globs) and must never see the user's host-auth token ג€” otherwise a
 194:  * compromised or hostile sender could exfiltrate it from a single tap.
 195:  * Closes Codex consultation 62 RED #1.
 196:  *
 197:  * Pattern mirrors [app.syncler.android.pluginhost.capabilities.NetworkBridge],
 198:  * which also builds its own unauthenticated client for the same reason on
 199:  * the WebView-based renderer path.
 200:  */
 201: @Singleton
 202: class TemplateActionRunner @Inject constructor() {
 203:     private val httpClient: OkHttpClient by lazy {
 204:         OkHttpClient.Builder()
 205:             .connectionSpecs(
 206:                 if (BuildConfig.DEBUG) {
 207:                     listOf(ConnectionSpec.MODERN_TLS, ConnectionSpec.CLEARTEXT)
 208:                 } else {
 209:                     listOf(ConnectionSpec.MODERN_TLS)
 210:                 },
 211:             )
 212:             .build()
 213:     }
 214: 
 215:     suspend fun post(endpoint: String, payloadJson: String) {
 216:         withContext(Dispatchers.IO) {
 217:             // Release builds reject cleartext outright. NetworkBridge does
 218:             // the same check; we mirror it here so a leaked-template
 219:             // manifest with an http:// endpoint can't fall through to a
 220:             // cleartext POST on production.
 221:             val schemeOk = endpoint.startsWith("https://") ||
 222:                 (BuildConfig.DEBUG && endpoint.startsWith("http://"))
 223:             if (!schemeOk) {
 224:                 Timber.tag(TAG).w("template action POST %s blocked: non-HTTPS", endpoint)
 225:                 return@withContext
 226:             }
 227:             runCatching {
 228:                 val request = Request.Builder()
 229:                     .url(endpoint)
 230:                     .post(payloadJson.toRequestBody(JSON_MEDIA))

 succeeded in 300ms:

   5: import javax.inject.Singleton
   6: import kotlin.math.min
   7: import kotlinx.coroutines.CoroutineScope
   8: import kotlinx.coroutines.Dispatchers
   9: import kotlinx.coroutines.Job
  10: import kotlinx.coroutines.SupervisorJob
  11: import kotlinx.coroutines.delay
  12: import kotlinx.coroutines.flow.MutableSharedFlow
  13: import kotlinx.coroutines.flow.SharedFlow
  14: import kotlinx.coroutines.flow.asSharedFlow
  15: import kotlinx.coroutines.launch
  16: import okhttp3.OkHttpClient
  17: import okhttp3.Request
  18: import okhttp3.Response
  19: import okhttp3.sse.EventSource
  20: import okhttp3.sse.EventSourceListener
  21: import okhttp3.sse.EventSources
  22: import org.json.JSONObject
  23: import timber.log.Timber
  24: 
  25: /**
  26:  * Phase 2: server event stream client.
  27:  *
  28:  * Opens a Server-Sent Events stream to `GET /v1/events` while the app
  29:  * is in the foreground, and translates incoming events into a
  30:  * [SharedFlow<ServerEvent>] that feature-layer collectors subscribe to.
  31:  *
  32:  * Lifecycle: [start] is idempotent (no-op if a stream is already open
  33:  * or a reconnect is scheduled); [stop] cancels the current stream AND
  34:  * any pending reconnect cleanly. The Android UI layer binds these to
  35:  * `Lifecycle.Event.ON_RESUME` / `ON_PAUSE`.
  36:  *
  37:  * Reactive freshness model replaces the V1 polling loop:
  38:  *  - SSE delivers hints (inbox.changed, state.changed, dismiss) while
  39:  *    the app is in foreground.
  40:  *  - Transient network failures auto-reconnect with exponential backoff
  41:  *    (Codex consultation 56 RED #13) so a network flip doesn't strand
  42:  *    the user until the next lifecycle event.
  43:  *  - 401 (bootstrap token / device-revoked / other auth failure) is
  44:  *    treated as terminal: the manager calls `onAuthFailure` so the
  45:  *    auth layer can clear the session and route to login.
  46:  *  - FCM remains the background-wakeup path (Doze kills any
  47:  *    long-lived stream the moment the app backgrounds anyway).
  48:  */
  49: @Singleton
  50: class EventStreamManager @Inject constructor(
  51:     private val httpClient: OkHttpClient,
  52:     private val tokenProviders: Set<@JvmSuppressWildcards AuthTokenProvider>,
  53:     private val authFailureHandler: AuthFailureHandler,
  54: ) {
  55:     private val _events = MutableSharedFlow<ServerEvent>(
  56:         replay = 0,
  57:         extraBufferCapacity = 64,
  58:     )
  59:     val events: SharedFlow<ServerEvent> = _events.asSharedFlow()
  60: 
  61:     /**
  62:      * Emits Unit once the SSE handshake actually completes (server
  63:      * acknowledged the subscription). Collectors use this to do a
  64:      * "catchup" refresh AFTER the stream is open ג€” closes the small
  65:      * race where `start()` returns before subscription is live and an
  66:      * event landed during that gap is missed (Codex consultation 56
  67:      * RED #9).
  68:      */
  69:     private val _streamReady = MutableSharedFlow<Unit>(
  70:         replay = 0,
  71:         extraBufferCapacity = 4,
  72:     )
  73:     val streamReady: SharedFlow<Unit> = _streamReady.asSharedFlow()
  74: 
  75:     /**
  76:      * Single monitor that serializes every lifecycle/state transition:
  77:      * `start`, `stop`, `openStream`, `scheduleReconnect`, and the
  78:      * mutating portions of the SSE listener callbacks (`onOpen`,
  79:      * `onClosed`, `onFailure`). Closes the Codex consultation 58
  80:      * compound-transition race where stop() interleaved with openStream()
  81:      * could leave `wantRunning == true` with `current == null` and no
  82:      * reconnect scheduled.
  83:      *
  84:      * The lock is uncontended in the common case (one open stream, one
  85:      * lifecycle thread, occasional okhttp dispatcher callbacks) and
  86:      * never held across a suspend point ג€” all suspending work (`delay`
  87:      * in reconnect) happens outside the lock.
  88:      */
  89:     private val lifecycleLock = Any()
  90: 
  91:     /**
  92:      * The EventSource we currently consider "ours". Mutated only while
  93:      * holding [lifecycleLock]; reads are also locked except for the
  94:      * identity check in `onEvent` (the high-frequency hot path), where
  95:      * volatility is enough ג€” a stale read just drops the event safely.
  96:      */
  97:     @Volatile
  98:     private var current: EventSource? = null
  99: 
 100:     /**
 101:      * Tracks whether we've been asked to be running by lifecycle.
 102:      * Reconnect attempts only fire while this is true so a backgrounded
 103:      * app doesn't spin up new streams via the retry path.
 104:      */
 105:     @Volatile
 106:     private var wantRunning: Boolean = false
 107: 
 108:     /**
 109:      * Active reconnect job. Cancelled on `stop()` so a queued retry
 110:      * after pause doesn't open a stream the user can't see.
 111:      */
 112:     private var reconnectJob: Job? = null
 113: 
 114:     /**
 115:      * Current reconnect attempt count. Reset on successful onOpen.
 116:      * Used to compute exponential backoff (1s, 2s, 4s, 8s, 16s, 30s cap).
 117:      */
 118:     @Volatile
 119:     private var reconnectAttempt: Int = 0
 120: 
 121:     private val scope = CoroutineScope(SupervisorJob() + Dispatchers.IO)
 122: 
 123:     private val sseFactory by lazy {
 124:         val sseClient = httpClient.newBuilder()
 125:             .readTimeout(0, TimeUnit.MILLISECONDS)
 126:             .retryOnConnectionFailure(true)
 127:             .build()
 128:         EventSources.createFactory(sseClient)
 129:     }
 130: 
 131:     /**
 132:      * Open a stream if one isn't already open. Returns immediately;
 133:      * the stream runs in the background and surfaces events through
 134:      * the [events] flow. Collectors that need a "stream is now live"
 135:      * signal observe [streamReady].
 136:      */
 137:     fun start() {
 138:         synchronized(lifecycleLock) {
 139:             wantRunning = true
 140:             openStreamLocked()
 141:         }
 142:     }
 143: 
 144:     /** Cancel the current stream + any pending reconnect. */
 145:     fun stop() {
 146:         val prev = synchronized(lifecycleLock) {
 147:             wantRunning = false
 148:             reconnectJob?.cancel()
 149:             reconnectJob = null
 150:             reconnectAttempt = 0
 151:             val p = current
 152:             current = null
 153:             p
 154:         }
 155:         prev?.cancel()
 156:         Timber.tag(TAG).i("event stream closed")
 157:     }
 158: 
 159:     private fun openStreamLocked() {
 160:         if (!wantRunning) return
 161:         if (current != null) return
 162:         val token = tokenProviders.firstNotNullOfOrNull { it.currentToken() }
 163:         if (token.isNullOrBlank()) {
 164:             Timber.tag(TAG).w("openStreamLocked() called without a session token; ignoring")
 165:             return
 166:         }
 167:         val request = Request.Builder()
 168:             .url(BuildConfig.SERVER_BASE_URL.trimEnd('/') + "/v1/events")
 169:             .header("Authorization", "Bearer $token")
 170:             .header("Accept", "text/event-stream")
 171:             .build()
 172:         // Listener is per-stream so it captures the token used for this
 173:         // handshake; the 401 path passes that token back through
 174:         // AuthFailureHandler so the auth layer can ignore stale 401s
 175:         // for tokens the session no longer holds (Codex 57 RED #12).
 176:         // newEventSource returns immediately; the actual handshake runs
 177:         // asynchronously on the okhttp dispatcher.
 178:         val source = sseFactory.newEventSource(request, makeListener(token))
 179:         current = source
 180:         Timber.tag(TAG).i("event stream opening (attempt=%d)", reconnectAttempt)
 181:     }
 182: 
 183:     private fun scheduleReconnectLocked() {
 184:         if (!wantRunning) return
 185:         if (reconnectJob?.isActive == true) return
 186:         val attempt = ++reconnectAttempt
 187:         // Exponential backoff: 1s, 2s, 4s, 8s, 16s, capped at 30s.
 188:         val delayMs = min(1_000L * (1L shl (attempt - 1).coerceAtMost(5)), 30_000L)
 189:         Timber.tag(TAG).i("scheduling SSE reconnect attempt=%d in %dms", attempt, delayMs)
 190:         reconnectJob = scope.launch {
 191:             delay(delayMs)
 192:             synchronized(lifecycleLock) {
 193:                 // Retire ourselves before opening the new stream. Otherwise
 194:                 // the retry coroutine's Job remains isActive while we call
 195:                 // openStreamLocked, and if the just-opened stream fails
 196:                 // synchronously its onFailure callback would hit the
 197:                 // `reconnectJob?.isActive == true` guard above and silently
 198:                 // skip scheduling the next retry ג€” leaving the user with
 199:                 // `wantRunning=true, current=null, no reconnect` until a
 200:                 // lifecycle event. (Codex consultation 59 RED.)
 201:                 reconnectJob = null
 202:                 if (wantRunning) openStreamLocked()
 203:             }
 204:         }
 205:     }
 206: 
 207:     private fun makeListener(token: String) = object : EventSourceListener() {
 208:         override fun onOpen(eventSource: EventSource, response: Response) {
 209:             val accepted = synchronized(lifecycleLock) {
 210:                 if (current !== eventSource) false
 211:                 else {
 212:                     reconnectAttempt = 0
 213:                     true
 214:                 }
 215:             }
 216:             if (!accepted) return
 217:             Timber.tag(TAG).d("SSE open (status=%d)", response.code)
 218:             // Emit outside the lock ג€” collectors may do work in their
 219:             // tryEmit handler; no need to hold the lifecycle lock across.
 220:             _streamReady.tryEmit(Unit)
 221:         }
 222: 
 223:         override fun onEvent(eventSource: EventSource, id: String?, type: String?, data: String) {
 224:             // Hot path: lock-free identity check. A stale read drops the
 225:             // event safely; correctness is preserved by the mutating
 226:             // callbacks which take the lock.
 227:             if (current !== eventSource) return
 228:             val parsed = ServerEvent.parse(type, data)
 229:             if (parsed == null) {
 230:                 Timber.tag(TAG).w("ignoring SSE event with unknown/bad payload: type=%s", type)
 231:                 return
 232:             }
 233:             val accepted = _events.tryEmit(parsed)
 234:             if (!accepted) {
 235:                 Timber.tag(TAG).w("SSE event dropped ג€” buffer full: %s", type)
 236:             }
 237:         }
 238: 
 239:         override fun onClosed(eventSource: EventSource) {
 240:             synchronized(lifecycleLock) {
 241:                 if (current !== eventSource) return@synchronized
 242:                 current = null
 243:                 Timber.tag(TAG).i("SSE closed by server")
 244:                 if (wantRunning) scheduleReconnectLocked()
 245:             }
 246:         }
 247: 
 248:         override fun onFailure(eventSource: EventSource, t: Throwable?, response: Response?) {
 249:             var terminal401 = false
 250:             synchronized(lifecycleLock) {
 251:                 if (current !== eventSource) return@synchronized
 252:                 current = null
 253:                 val code = response?.code
 254:                 terminal401 = (code == 401)
 255:                 if (terminal401) {
 256:                     Timber.tag(TAG).w("SSE rejected with 401; signalling auth failure")
 257:                 } else {
 258:                     Timber.tag(TAG).w(t, "SSE failure (status=%s); will retry", code)
 259:                 }
 260:                 // Do NOT short-circuit reconnect on 401. Two cases:
 261:                 //  - Stale 401 (session token rolled by a fast re-login):
 262:                 //    the next reconnect picks up the new token and
 263:                 //    succeeds. AuthRepository.onAuthFailure verifies the
 264:                 //    token is still current before logging out.
 265:                 //  - Real terminal 401: AuthRepository.onAuthFailure
 266:                 //    triggers session.logout(), which clears the token.
 267:                 //    The next reconnect attempt sees a null token and
 268:                 //    no-ops; lifecycle teardown (InboxScreen ON_PAUSE
 269:                 //    when AuthScreen takes over) sets wantRunning=false.
 270:                 // Closes Codex consultation 58 concern: a stale 401 must
 271:                 // not strand SSE in a stopped state for an unrelated
 272:                 // session that's still alive.
 273:                 if (wantRunning) scheduleReconnectLocked()
 274:             }
 275:             // Auth handler call happens outside the lock ג€” it does
 276:             // scope.launch internally and we don't want any handler
 277:             // ordering effects to hold the lifecycle lock.
 278:             if (terminal401) {
 279:                 authFailureHandler.onAuthFailure(token)
 280:             }
 281:         }
 282:     }
 283: 
 284:     private companion object {
 285:         const val TAG = "EventStream"
 286:     }
 287: }
 288: 
 289: /**
 290:  * Implemented by the auth layer (`AuthRepository` is the production
 291:  * binding). EventStreamManager calls [onAuthFailure] when the server
 292:  * rejects the SSE handshake with 401 ג€” the auth layer is responsible
 293:  * for clearing the session and surfacing the login UI.
 294:  *
 295:  * [failedToken] is the bearer token that triggered the 401. The
 296:  * implementation MUST verify this still matches the session's current
 297:  * token before logging out ג€” otherwise a stale 401 from a stream that
 298:  * was already replaced (e.g., after a fast re-login) could wipe the
 299:  * newer session (Codex consultation 57 RED #12).
 300:  *
 301:  * Defined as an interface in `:core:network` so this module doesn't
 302:  * depend back on `:core:auth`.
 303:  */
 304: interface AuthFailureHandler {
 305:     fun onAuthFailure(failedToken: String)
 306: }
 307: 
 308: /**
 309:  * A decoded SSE event from `/v1/events`. The server publishes hints
 310:  * (not authoritative data) ג€” collectors react by calling the existing
 311:  * REST endpoints to fetch the actual content.
 312:  */
 313: sealed class ServerEvent {
 314:     /** A new inbox message landed for this user. Pull the inbox. */
 315:     data class InboxChanged(val messageId: String?, val sentAt: String?) : ServerEvent()
 316: 
 317:     /** The encrypted user-state blob changed. Pull /v1/state. */
 318:     data class StateChanged(val version: Int) : ServerEvent()
 319: 
 320:     /** Another device dismissed a message. Update local state. */
 321:     data class Dismiss(val messageId: String, val sourceDeviceId: String?) : ServerEvent()
 322: 
 323:     /** A live card was created or updated. */
 324:     data class CardUpsert(val data: String) : ServerEvent()
 325: 
 326:     /** A live card was deleted. */
 327:     data class CardDelete(val senderId: String, val cardKey: String) : ServerEvent()
 328: 
 329:     companion object {
 330:         fun parse(type: String?, data: String): ServerEvent? = runCatching {
 331:             val obj = JSONObject(data)
 332:             when (type) {
 333:                 "inbox.changed" -> InboxChanged(
 334:                     messageId = obj.optString("message_id").takeIf { it.isNotEmpty() },
 335:                     sentAt = obj.optString("sent_at").takeIf { it.isNotEmpty() },
 336:                 )
 337:                 "state.changed" -> StateChanged(version = obj.getInt("version"))
 338:                 "dismiss" -> Dismiss(
 339:                     messageId = obj.getString("message_id"),
 340:                     sourceDeviceId = obj.optString("source_device_id").takeIf { it.isNotEmpty() },

 468: class TemplateObject(BaseModel):
 469:     """The Phase 3a template manifest block. Senders ship one of these
 470:     instead of a JS bundle when they want native Compose rendering."""
 471:     layout: str
 472:     fields: dict[str, TemplateField]
 473:     actions: list[TemplateAction] = []
 474: 
 475:     @field_validator("layout")
 476:     @classmethod
 477:     def validate_layout(cls, value: str) -> str:
 478:         if value not in _TEMPLATE_LAYOUTS:
 479:             raise ValueError(
 480:                 f"unknown template layout {value!r}; supported: {sorted(_TEMPLATE_LAYOUTS)}",
 481:             )
 482:         return value
 483: 
 484:     @model_validator(mode="after")
 485:     def validate_fields_for_layout(self) -> "TemplateObject":
 486:         required = _LAYOUT_REQUIRED_FIELDS.get(self.layout, frozenset())
 487:         optional = _LAYOUT_OPTIONAL_FIELDS.get(self.layout, frozenset())
 488:         allowed = required | optional
 489:         missing = required - self.fields.keys()
 490:         if missing:
 491:             raise ValueError(
 492:                 f"layout {self.layout!r} requires fields {sorted(missing)}",
 493:             )
 494:         extra = self.fields.keys() - allowed
 495:         if extra:
 496:             raise ValueError(
 497:                 f"layout {self.layout!r} does not accept fields {sorted(extra)}",
 498:             )
 499:         # Action ids must be unique within a template so the client can route
 500:         # an action tap unambiguously.
 501:         action_ids = [a.id for a in self.actions]
 502:         if len(action_ids) != len(set(action_ids)):
 503:             raise ValueError(f"duplicate action ids in template")
 504:         return self

 510:     version: Annotated[str, Field(min_length=1, max_length=64)]
 511:     manifest_hash: str  # base64 32 bytes
 512:     bundle_hash: str    # base64 32 bytes
 513:     signature: str      # base64 64 bytes Ed25519 (bundle signature)
 514:     signed_bundle_url: str
 515:     capabilities: list[str]
 516:     endpoints: list[str]
 517:     # Phase 3a. Defaults to "script" for backwards compat with senders
 518:     # published before the template renderer existed ג€” their canonical
 519:     # publish envelope does not include this field, so the conditional
 520:     # serialization in `_publish_envelope` keeps their signature valid.
 521:     renderer: Literal["script", "template"] = "script"
 522:     template: TemplateObject | None = None
 523:     # Phase 3b: card_type ("event" or "live") and optional card_key_path
 524:     # for live cards.

 527:     sender_signature: str  # base64 Ed25519 over canonical publish body
 528: 
 529:     @field_validator("manifest_hash")
 530:     @classmethod
 531:     def validate_manifest_hash(cls, value: str) -> str:
 532:         decode_base64(value, field_name="manifest_hash", exact=32)
 533:         return value
 534: 
 535:     @field_validator("bundle_hash")
 536:     @classmethod
 537:     def validate_bundle_hash(cls, value: str) -> str:
 538:         decode_base64(value, field_name="bundle_hash", exact=32)
 539:         return value
 540: 
 541:     @field_validator("signature")
 542:     @classmethod
 543:     def validate_signature(cls, value: str) -> str:
 544:         decode_base64(value, field_name="signature", exact=64)
 545:         return value
 546: 
 547:     @field_validator("sender_signature")

 551:         return value
 552: 
 553:     @model_validator(mode="after")
 554:     def validate_renderer_template_pairing(self) -> "PluginPublishRequest":
 555:         # The pairing rules live here (not on TemplateObject) because the
 556:         # action-endpoint check needs the surrounding `endpoints` glob list.
 557:         if self.renderer == "template" and self.template is None:
 558:             raise ValueError("template required when renderer == 'template'")
 559:         if self.renderer == "script" and self.template is not None:
 560:             raise ValueError("template must be omitted when renderer == 'script'")
 561:         if self.template is not None:
 562:             for action in self.template.actions:
 563:                 if not any(
 564:                     _endpoint_pattern_matches(action.endpoint, p)
 565:                     for p in self.endpoints
 566:                 ):
 567:                     raise ValueError(
 568:                         f"action {action.id!r} endpoint {action.endpoint!r} "
 569:                         f"not allowed by declared endpoints",
 570:                     )
 571:         # Phase 3b: live cards MUST have a card_key_path to extract their
 572:         # stable identity from the payload.
 573:         if self.card_type == "live" and not self.card_key_path:
 574:             raise ValueError("card_key_path required when card_type == 'live'")
 575:         return self
 576: 
 577: 
 578: class PluginPublishResponse(BaseModel):
 579:     plugin_row_id: UUID
 580:     plugin_identifier: str
 581:     version: str
 582:     created_at: datetime
 583: 
 584: 
 585: class PluginLatestResponse(BaseModel):
 586:     plugin_row_id: UUID
 587:     sender_id: UUID
 588:     plugin_identifier: str
 589:     version: str
 590:     signed_bundle_url: str
 591:     manifest_hash: str
 592:     bundle_hash: str
 593:     signature: str
 594:     capabilities: list[str]
 595:     endpoints: list[str]
 596:     created_at: datetime
 597:     # M11.4: when the row is revoked, surface why so devices can render
 598:     # differentiated UX (silent for ``superseded``, security alert for
 599:     # ``compromised``, neutral "unavailable" for ``sender_disabled``).
 600:     # The /latest endpoint filters revoked rows out so these are always
 601:     # null there; the /by-id endpoint (used for historical lookups by
 602:     # plugin_row_id) returns whatever the row's current revoke state is.
 603:     revoked_at: datetime | None = None
 604:     revocation_reason: str | None = None
 605:     # Phase 3a. Defaults to "script" so pre-Phase-3a stored rows (where the
 606:     # backfilled server default fills NULL with "script") and pre-Phase-3a
 607:     # clients (which ignore the field) both see the WebView path.
 608:     renderer: Literal["script", "template"] = "script"
 609:     template: TemplateObject | None = None
 610:     # Phase 3b: card_type ("event" or "live") and optional card_key_path.
 611:     card_type: Literal["event", "live"] = "event"
 612:     card_key_path: str | None = None
 613: 
 614: 
 615: # M11.4: classified revocation reasons. Devices use this to decide UX:
 616: # - ``superseded``: silent; show in update prompts.
 617: # - ``compromised``: refuse to execute; show security alert.
 618: # - ``sender_disabled``: stop rendering; show neutral "unavailable".
 619: # - ``unspecified``: legacy revokes (pre-M11.4) where no reason was given;
 620: #   conservative client treats this as ``compromised`` until clarified.
 621: REVOCATION_REASONS = frozenset({"superseded", "compromised", "sender_disabled", "unspecified"})
 622: 
 623: 
 624: class PluginRevokeRequest(BaseModel):
 625:     sender_id: UUID
 626:     plugin_row_id: UUID
 627:     sender_signature: str  # base64 Ed25519 over canonical body
 628:     # Optional in V1 for backwards compatibility with the M8.1 contract;
 629:     # senders SHOULD always supply one. Missing reason ג†’ stored as null;
 630:     # client code interprets null as ``unspecified``.
 631:     reason: str | None = None
 632: 
 633:     @field_validator("sender_signature")
 634:     @classmethod
 635:     def validate_sender_signature(cls, value: str) -> str:
 636:         decode_base64(value, field_name="sender_signature", exact=64)
 637:         return value
 638: 
 639:     @field_validator("reason")
 640:     @classmethod
 641:     def validate_reason(cls, value: str | None) -> str | None:
 642:         if value is None:
 643:             return None
 644:         if value not in REVOCATION_REASONS:
 645:             raise ValueError(
 646:                 f"reason must be one of {sorted(REVOCATION_REASONS)}; got {value!r}"
 647:             )
 648:         return value

   1: # Syncler Roadmap
   2: 
   3: The Syncler platform is built and released in milestones. **V1 is what ships today**; the items below it are sequenced by platform dependencies (security primitives first, capability surface second, scaling third, UX last).
   4: 
   5: This file is the public roadmap. Internal implementation phases (Phase 0 / 1 / 2 / 3 / 4) used in the codebase and consultations track *how V1 was built*; this document tracks *what comes next*.
   6: 
   7: ## V1 ג€” Foundational milestone (shipped)
   8: 
   9: - [x] Device-bound JWTs with server-side revocation enforcement
  10: - [x] Synced pairing via the encrypted user-state blob (M7 CAS state)
  11: - [x] Server-Sent Events stream for real-time hint delivery (`inbox.changed`, `state.changed`, `dismiss`, `card.upsert`, `card.delete`)
  12: - [x] Native Material 3 template renderer (no-JS plugins via JSONPath manifest)
  13: - [x] Persistent, upsertable Live Cards with server-enforced 48h TTL + sequence-monotone updates
  14: - [x] Host-owned plugin settings sheet (sender mute, plugin revoke)
  15: - [x] Cross-device dismiss filter (server-side `DeliveryStatus` join)
  16: - [x] Per-device envelope auth-token isolation for template-renderer action POSTs
  17: 
  18: ## V1.5 ג€” Plugin runtime + key hygiene
  19: 
  20: 1. **Multi-process plugin host.** Move JS plugin execution to a dedicated Android process via AIDL/Binder. Isolates a crashing or runaway plugin from the host UI process and gives us a clean ProcessRecord boundary for the OS to kill independently.
  21: 2. **Native Kotlin plugin runtime (out-of-process).** A second plugin format alongside the JS bundle: a signed AAR loaded into the isolated process. Performance + platform-API parity for plugin authors who want a native experience, with the IPC boundary preventing in-process ClassLoader poisoning.
  22: 3. **Master-key rotation.** UX + protocol for rotating the user's 32-byte master key without losing access to historical state. Required before per-device encryption (#4) lands.
  23: 4. **Per-device envelope encryption.** Senders encrypt the payload separately for each of the user's enrolled devices, keyed by per-device public keys instead of the shared user master key. Enables forward secrecy and immediate per-device revocation without rotating user-wide keys.
  24: 5. **Durable nonce-replay protection.** Move the per-sender nonce registry from in-memory to Postgres so a worker restart can't accept a replayed envelope.
  25: 
  26: ## V2 ג€” Capability surface
  27: 
  28: 6. **Plugin capability expansion.** Add `camera`, `storage`, `file`, `location`, `gallery` to the bridge with per-grant prompts. Each capability lands with its own audit-log + user-visible permission dialog.
  29: 7. **`message.respond` + `showNotification`.** Promote action callbacks from a fire-and-forget POST to a request/response handshake the plugin can await. Add a `showNotification` bridge so non-inbox-mode flows (background alerts) work.
  30: 8. **Template renderer layouts.** Expand beyond `standard_card` to `compact_row`, `score_card`, and a handful of other layouts driven by data-class types. Each new layout ships with golden render tests.
  31: 9. **Script-fast runtime (Javy/QuickJS).** A lighter, non-WebView execution mode for purely logic-heavy plugins that don't need DOM. Faster cold-start and less memory than the current WebView path.
  32: 
  33: ## V3 ג€” Two-way + scaling
  34: 
  35: 10. **WebSocket two-way channel.** Bidirectional, low-latency channel between plugins and their backends; covers chat, live cursors, presence. Complements but does not replace the SSE hint channel for V1's pull-then-render model.
  36: 11. **`platform.live.subscribe(...)` for script plugins.** API for a script bundle to subscribe to a named feed and receive incremental updates without polling.
  37: 12. **Field-level live subscriptions on templates.** Update specific template fields without re-rendering the whole card ג€” the live-card path today is whole-card upsert; this adds a finer grain.
  38: 13. **Redis pub/sub for SSE scaling.** Move the in-process event bus to a shared backplane so the SSE fanout works across multiple FastAPI workers and pods.
  39: 
  40: ## V4 ג€” UX polish
  41: 
  42: 14. **Guided lost-device rotation flow.** Click-through UX for: revoke lost device ג†’ re-pair on trusted devices ג†’ rotate master key (depends on V1.5 #3). Today the user does steps 1ג€“2 by hand; this automates the sequence.
  43: 15. **Per-plugin user preferences.** Notification cadence, label overrides, delivery-window scheduling, do-not-disturb integration ג€” all surfaced from the host's settings sheet without plugin-side code.
  44: 
  45: ---
  46: 
  47: Cross-reference: implementation-level work tracked in `.triad/50-agreement-and-plan.md`. Plugin authors should read `docs/integration-guide.md` and `docs/crypto-spec.md` ג€” those two documents are the public contract.

 succeeded in 279ms:
 220: ## 8. Live Cards (Phase 3b)
 221: 
 222: Live cards are persistent, upsertable units identified by `(sender_id, user_id, card_key)`. The encrypted payload uses the same AES-256-GCM primitive as messages, but with a richer AAD that binds the card-specific metadata. Upsert and delete each have their own Ed25519 envelope distinct from the message envelope.
 223: 
 224: ### 8.1 Live Card AAD
 225: 
 226: Canonical JSON, UTF-8, sorted keys, compact separators (same encoder as ֲ§4):
 227: 
 228: ```json
 229: {
 230:   "card_key": "...",
 231:   "card_type": "live",
 232:   "expires_at": "<ISO8601 UTC with Z suffix>",
 233:   "plugin_id": "...",
 234:   "sender_id": "...",
 235:   "user_id": "...",
 236:   "sequence_number": <integer JSON literal>
 237: }
 238: ```
 239: 
 240: `card_type` is always the string `"live"` (the field exists so the AAD shape can extend cleanly when future card types land ג€” e.g. ephemeral or scheduled cards). `sequence_number` is emitted as a JSON integer literal (no quotes); senders MUST NOT stringify it. `expires_at` MUST use the `Z` UTC suffix (not `+00:00`) so SDK and server agree on the canonical bytes.
 241: 
 242: The AAD binds the ciphertext to a specific (sender, user, plugin, card, sequence, expiry) tuple. A replay of an older sequence or a substitution of one card's ciphertext under another's metadata will fail AES-GCM tag verification on decrypt.
 243: 
 244: ### 8.2 Live Card Upsert Envelope (Ed25519 signing input)
 245: 
 246: Canonical JSON for the sender's `envelope_signature` on `POST /v1/cards/upsert`:
 247: 
 248: ```json
 249: {
 250:   "card_key": "...",
 251:   "card_type": "live",
 252:   "encrypted_payload": "<base64 ciphertext_with_tag, no nonce prefix>",
 253:   "expires_at": "<ISO8601 UTC with Z suffix>",
 254:   "nonce": "<base64 12-byte nonce>",
 255:   "plugin_id": "...",
 256:   "sender_id": "...",
 257:   "sequence_number": <integer JSON literal>,
 258:   "user_id": "..."
 259: }
 260: ```
 261: 
 262: The server constructs the same canonical bytes from the request body (via `assemble_envelope` in `server/app/routers/cards.py`) and verifies against the registered sender's public key. UUIDs MUST be canonicalized to lowercase no-brace form before signing (`str(uuid.UUID(value))`) ג€” the SDK normalizes via `_canon_uuid` to prevent sender-side self-401s on uppercase or braced input.
 263: 
 264: ### 8.3 Live Card Delete Envelope (Ed25519 signing input)
 265: 
 266: Canonical JSON for `POST /v1/cards/delete`:
 267: 
 268: ```json
 269: {
 270:   "card_key": "...",
 271:   "sender_id": "...",
 272:   "user_id": "..."
 273: }
 274: ```
 275: 
 276: **`user_id` is REQUIRED in the envelope.** Without it, a delete signature valid for one user's card could be replayed against another user's card with a coincidentally matching `(sender_id, card_key)` ג€” the table is uniquely keyed on `(sender_id, user_id, card_key)`, so the lookup would otherwise be ambiguous. (Codex consultation 62 security finding.) The server matches the exact triple before deleting; mismatched triples no-op silently and still publish a `card.delete` SSE event so all of the user's devices clear any stale local copy.
 277: 
 278: ### 8.4 Test Vectors
 279: 
 280: Live-card vectors live alongside the rest in `server/tests/test_crypto.py` (round-trip) and `android/core/crypto/.../SpecVectorsTest.kt` (Android cross-check). The canonical envelope bytes for upsert/delete are asserted in `server/tests/test_phase3.py` via signature-verification round trips against `app/routers/cards.py:_build_upsert_envelope_bytes` and `_build_delete_envelope_bytes`.
 281: 
 282: ## Python Reference Snippets
 283: 
 284: ```python
 285: import json
 286: from cryptography.hazmat.primitives import hashes
 287: from cryptography.hazmat.primitives.ciphers.aead import AESGCM
 288: from cryptography.hazmat.primitives.kdf.hkdf import HKDF
 289: 
 290: def derive_pairing_key(master_key: bytes, sender_id: bytes) -> bytes:
 291:     return HKDF(
 292:         algorithm=hashes.SHA256(),
 293:         length=32,
 294:         salt=sender_id,
 295:         info=b"syncler-v1-pairing-key:" + sender_id,
 296:     ).derive(master_key)
 297: 
 298: def assemble_aad(fields: dict[str, object]) -> bytes:
 299:     return json.dumps(fields, ensure_ascii=True, separators=(",", ":"), sort_keys=True).encode("utf-8")
 300: 
 301: def decrypt(pairing_key: bytes, wire: bytes, aad: bytes) -> bytes:
 302:     nonce = wire[:12]
 303:     ciphertext_with_tag = wire[12:]
 304:     return AESGCM(pairing_key).decrypt(nonce, ciphertext_with_tag, aad)
 305: 
 306: # --- Live cards (ֲ§8) -----------------------------------------------------

 309:     *,

 314:     sequence_number: int,

 316: ) -> bytes:
 317:     return json.dumps(
 318:         {

 320:             "card_type": "live",

 322:             "plugin_id": str(plugin_id),
 323:             "sender_id": str(sender_id),
 324:             "user_id": str(user_id),
 325:             "sequence_number": sequence_number,
 326:         },
 327:         ensure_ascii=True,
 328:         separators=(",", ":"),
 329:         sort_keys=True,
 330:     ).encode("utf-8")
 331:

 335:     user_id: str,
 336:     plugin_id: str,
 337:     card_key: str,
 338:     encrypted_payload_b64: str,
 339:     nonce_b64: str,
 340:     sequence_number: int,

 342: ) -> bytes:
 343:     return json.dumps(
 344:         {
 345:             "card_key": card_key,
 346:             "card_type": "live",
 347:             "encrypted_payload": encrypted_payload_b64,
 348:             "expires_at": expires_at.isoformat().replace("+00:00", "Z"),
 349:             "nonce": nonce_b64,
 350:             "plugin_id": str(plugin_id),
 351:             "sender_id": str(sender_id),
 352:             "sequence_number": sequence_number,
 353:             "user_id": str(user_id),
 354:         },
 355:         ensure_ascii=True,
 356:         separators=(",", ":"),
 357:         sort_keys=True,
 358:     ).encode("utf-8")

 361:     *,
 362:     sender_id: str,
 363:     user_id: str,
 364:     card_key: str,
 365: ) -> bytes:
 366:     return json.dumps(
 367:         {
 368:             "card_key": card_key,
 369:             "sender_id": str(sender_id),
 370:             "user_id": str(user_id),

 241: 
 242: ### 5.1 Native Template Renderer
 243: 
 244: Set `renderer="template"` to ship a Compose-rendered native card instead of a JS bundle. The publish call looks like this:
 245: 
 246: ```python
 247: response = client.publish_plugin(
 248:     plugin_identifier="com.example.weather",
 249:     version="1.0.0",
 250:     manifest_hash=hashlib.sha256(b"manifest-placeholder").digest(),
 251:     bundle_hash=hashlib.sha256(b"unused-for-template").digest(),
 252:     bundle_signature=b"\x00" * 64,            # ignored for template
 253:     signed_bundle_url="https://example.com/unused",  # ignored for template
 254:     capabilities=[],
 255:     endpoints=["https://example.com/api/*"],
 256:     renderer="template",
 257:     template={
 258:         "layout": "standard_card",
 259:         "fields": {
 260:             "title":    {"path": "$.title"},
 261:             "subtitle": {"path": "$.subtitle"},
 262:             "body":     {"path": "$.body"},
 263:         },
 264:         "actions": [
 265:             {"id": "ack", "label": "Acknowledge", "endpoint": "https://example.com/api/ack"},
 266:         ],
 267:     },
 268: )
 269: ```
 270: 
 271: **JSONPath dialect.** Only `$.field(.subfield)*` is accepted. No array indexing (`$.items[0]`), no wildcards (`$.*`), no filters (`$.items[?(@.x>0)]`). Field-name segments must match `[A-Za-z_][A-Za-z0-9_]*`. The server rejects manifests with malformed paths at publish time, and the client-side resolver returns `null` for malformed input as a defense-in-depth.
 272: 
 273: **Layouts.** V1 ships one layout:
 274: 
 275: | Layout | Required fields | Optional fields | Notes |
 276: |---|---|---|---|
 277: | `standard_card` | `title` | `subtitle`, `body` | All values rendered as plain text via Compose `Text`. No markdown / HTML / link interpretation ג€” a hostile payload value cannot inject a clickable link. |
 278: 
 279: Additional layouts (`compact_row`, `score_card`, etc.) are deferred to a future phase.
 280: 
 281: **Actions.** Each action is a button on the card. When tapped, the host POSTs the **full decrypted payload as `application/json`** to `endpoint`. No `Authorization` header is attached ג€” the host explicitly uses an unauthenticated HTTP client for action POSTs so the user's Syncler bearer token never reaches your plugin endpoint (security boundary). If you need request authentication, HMAC the body using a sender-specific secret your backend knows out of band, or rely on TLS + endpoint allowlisting alone.
 282: 
 283: **Validation rules** the publish endpoint enforces (returns 422 otherwise):
 284: 
 285: - `layout` is in the supported set.
 286: - Required fields for the layout are present.
 287: - No fields outside the layout's allowed set.
 288: - Every `path` matches the JSONPath regex.
 289: - Every `action.endpoint` matches at least one of your declared `endpoints` globs (the same glob syntax that gates `platform.network.fetch` in script renderers).
 290: - Every `action.id` is unique within the template.
 291: 
 292: ### 5.2 Live Cards
 293: 
 294: Set `card_type="live"` to ship a persistent, upsertable card. The plugin manifest must also provide `card_key_path` ג€” a JSONPath into your decrypted payload that yields the stable identity for each card (e.g. `$.order_id`). This lets the inbox merge multiple upserts for the same logical card into one row.
 295: 
 296: ```python
 297: response = client.publish_plugin(
 298:     plugin_identifier="com.example.delivery",
 299:     version="1.0.0",
 300:     manifest_hash=hashlib.sha256(b"manifest").digest(),
 301:     bundle_hash=hashlib.sha256(open("dist/plugin.bundle.js","rb").read()).digest(),
 302:     bundle_signature=bytes.fromhex(manifest["signature"]),
 303:     signed_bundle_url="https://example.com/plugin.bundle.js",
 304:     capabilities=["network"],
 305:     endpoints=["https://example.com/api/*"],
 306:     card_type="live",
 307:     card_key_path="$.order_id",
 308: )
 309: ```
 310: 
 311: Live cards work with **either** renderer. The most common combo is `renderer="template"` + `card_type="live"` (delivery progress card with no JS).
 312: 
 313: #### Upserting a live card
 314: 
 315: ```python
 316: from syncler.crypto import assemble_aad, encrypt_payload
 317: from datetime import datetime, timedelta, UTC
 318: import os, json
 319: 
 320: expires_at = datetime.now(UTC) + timedelta(hours=12)
 321: plaintext = json.dumps({
 322:     "order_id": "order-456",
 323:     "title": "Pizza Delivery",
 324:     "body": "Out for delivery ג€” ETA 8 minutes",
 325: }).encode("utf-8")
 326: 
 327: aad = assemble_live_card_aad(
 328:     sender_id=client.sender_id,
 329:     user_id=user_id,
 330:     plugin_id=plugin_row_id,
 331:     card_key="order-456",
 332:     sequence_number=2,
 333:     expires_at=expires_at,
 334: )
 335: nonce = os.urandom(12)
 336: ciphertext = encrypt_payload(client.pairing_key, nonce, plaintext, aad)
 337: 
 338: client.upsert_card(
 339:     user_id=user_id,
 340:     plugin_id=plugin_row_id,
 341:     card_key="order-456",
 342:     encrypted_payload=ciphertext,
 343:     nonce=nonce,
 344:     sequence_number=2,
 345:     expires_at=expires_at,
 346: )
 347: ```
 348: 
 349: (See `docs/crypto-spec.md ֲ§8` for the exact `assemble_live_card_aad` byte shape ג€” the SDK helper builds the canonical JSON the device's AES-GCM decrypt will verify against.)
 350: 
 351: **Server-side gates on upsert** (return 4xx if violated ג€” see ֲ§9):
 352: 
 353: - **Active pairing required.** The `(sender_id, user_id)` pair must have a non-revoked `Pairing` row; otherwise 410. Mirrors the message-send path.
 354: - **Plugin must be active and live-type.** `Plugin.revoked_at IS NULL` and `card_type = "live"`; otherwise 410.
 355: - **TTL window.** `expires_at` must be strictly future (else 400) AND at most 48 hours from now (else 400). The cap is server-enforced and not negotiable.
 356: - **Sequence monotonicity.** New `sequence_number` must be strictly greater than the existing row's; else 409.
 357: - **Rate limit.** 1 upsert per second per `(sender_id, user_id, card_key)`; else 429.
 358: 
 359: The successful response triggers a `card.upsert` SSE event to every active device of the user, so foreground clients refresh within ~1s.
 360: 
 361: #### Deleting a live card
 362: 
 363: ```python
 364: client.delete_card(
 365:     user_id=user_id,
 366:     card_key="order-456",
 367: )
 368: ```
 369: 
 370: `user_id` is **required**. The canonical signed envelope binds `(sender_id, user_id, card_key)` ג€” without `user_id` in the signature, an attacker (or a coincidence: two users with the same `card_key` under the same sender) could be deleted by mistake. The delete endpoint matches exactly that triple in the row lookup.
 371: 
 372: ### 5.5 Revoking a plugin version
 373: 
 374: Revoke a single published plugin row when that exact version should be treated as inactive:
 375: 
 376: ```python
 377: client.revoke_plugin(
 378:     plugin_row_id="<plugin_row_id from publish_plugin>",
 379:     reason="superseded",
 380: )
 381: ```
 382: 
 383: `reason` is optional for legacy compatibility, but senders should always supply one of:
 384: 
 385: | Reason | Use when | Host UX |

 succeeded in 277ms:
 386: |---|---|---|
 387: | `superseded` | A newer version replaces this row. | Shows a subdued "newer version available" banner in detail; the historical bundle can still render. |
 388: | `compromised` | The bundle or signing key is unsafe. | Refuses to execute the bundle and shows a security banner with the decrypted payload fallback. |
 389: | `sender_disabled` | The sender/service is intentionally disabled. | Shows a neutral "sender unavailable" banner in detail; the historical bundle can still render. |
 390: | `unspecified` | You are migrating legacy tooling and cannot classify the revoke. | Shows a generic revoked banner; avoid using this for new revokes. |
 391: 
 392: The revoke request is signed by the SDK. The `reason` value is included in the signed envelope, so an intermediary cannot strip `compromised` down to a softer classification. Re-revoking a row keeps the original `revoked_at`; a higher-severity reason can promote the row, while downgrades are ignored.
 393: 
 394: ## 6. Sending a card (your backend, per event)
 395: 
 396: ```python
 397: # After pairing ג€” see SDK README for the pairing dance.
 398: client.set_pairing(user_id="...", pairing_key=b"...32-bytes...")
 399: 
 400: result = client.send_to(
 401:     user_uuid=user_uuid,
 402:     plugin_identifier="com.example.myapp",
 403:     plugin_id="<plugin_row_id from publish_plugin>",
 404:     payload={
 405:         "hostPreview": {
 406:             "title": "Something happened",
 407:             "subtitle": "Account A",
 408:             "summary": "Brief one-sentence context.",
 409:             "searchText": ["account-a", "alert"],
 410:         },
 411:         "item_id": "abc-123",
 412:         "body": "Details for the detail view.",
 413:         "action_label": "Acknowledge",
 414:     },
 415:     min_plugin_version="1.0.0",
 416: )
 417: ```
 418: 
 419: `ttl_seconds` defaults to 7 days. The server rejects envelopes that are already expired or more than 30 days in the future.
 420: 
 421: ## 7. The action callback endpoint
 422: 
 423: `https://your-app.example.com/api/action` accepts whatever body the host POSTs when the user taps an action button. The shape depends on which renderer you chose:
 424: 
 425: **Script renderer** ג€” your `onclick` handler builds the body via `platform.network.fetch`. In the ֲ§3 example that's:
 426: 
 427: ```http
 428: POST /api/action
 429: Content-Type: application/json
 430: 
 431: { "item_id": "...", "acted_at": "..." }
 432: ```
 433: 
 434: **Template renderer** ג€” the host POSTs the **full decrypted payload** as the body, verbatim. There's no JS hook to intervene. Your endpoint receives the whole payload JSON; pull whatever fields you need server-side. No `Authorization` header is added by the host (the user's Syncler bearer token never reaches your endpoint ג€” security boundary). If you need request authentication, HMAC the payload using a sender-specific secret your backend shares out of band with itself, or rely on TLS + endpoint allowlisting alone.
 435: 
 436: Note: the platform does **not** inject `device_id` into the body for you in V1. If you need to distinguish which device acted, include a sender-generated identifier in your payload and (for script renderer) have the plugin echo it back. For template renderer, your `card_key` (or any other field in the payload) serves the same dedupe role. Dedupe by `item_id` / `card_key` alone if a single tap is what you care about.
 437: 
 438: - Status 200 -> recorded.
 439: - Status 409 -> idempotent dedupe (already saw this item); platform may retry on transient network errors so be ready.
 440: - Status 4xx other -> platform surfaces a generic failure to the plugin's promise.
 441: 
 442: ```python
 443: # Flask example ג€” dedupe by item_id alone in V1.
 444: @app.post("/api/action")
 445: def action():
 446:     data = request.json
 447:     item_id = data["item_id"]
 448:     if Action.query.filter_by(item_id=item_id).first():
 449:         return "", 409
 450:     db.session.add(Action(item_id=item_id, acted_at=data["acted_at"]))
 451:     db.session.commit()
 452:     return "", 200
 453: ```
 454: 
 455: ## 8. Testing it end-to-end
 456: 
 457: 1. Install the Syncler Android app (`./gradlew :app:installDebug`).
 458: 2. Sign up + log in. The app auto-enrolls this device with the server.
 459: 3. From your backend, run a script that registers your sender and prints a pairing QR (see SDK README).
 460: 4. Tap **Pair sender** -> **Scan QR** in the Syncler app. Confirm the fingerprint matches what your script prints.
 461: 5. After confirming, the app shows your `user_id` and a `pairing_key_hex`. Copy both and feed them into your backend's `client.set_pairing(user_id, pairing_key=bytes.fromhex(...))` so it can encrypt for you.
 462: 6. Publish your plugin (`client.publish_plugin(...)`) ג€” save the `plugin_row_id`.
 463: 7. Run `client.send_to(...)` with a test payload.
 464: 8. The server pushes an `inbox.changed` event over the SSE stream the open app is subscribed to (foreground); the phone refreshes its inbox, decrypts the message, fetches your bundle (or applies your template manifest), and shows the native row within ~1s. If the app is backgrounded, FCM wakes it and the inbox refresh happens on the next foreground.
 465: 9. Tap the row to open the plugin-rendered detail view, then tap your action button.
 466: 10. Confirm your `/api/action` endpoint received the POST.
 467: 
 468: ## 9. Common errors
 469: 
 470: - **`401 invalid envelope signature`** ג€” your sender's Ed25519 key doesn't match the one registered. Re-check `private_key_path`.
 471: - **`410 plugin missing, revoked, or not owned by sender`** ג€” `plugin_id` (the row UUID) is wrong, or you accidentally used `plugin_identifier`. The two are distinct (see ֲ§5 vs ֲ§6).
 472: - **`410 recipient has no active devices`** ג€” the user has no enrolled device (signed up but never opened the app, or revoked all devices). FCM availability is *not* required; messages are stored regardless and pulled via `/v1/messages/inbox`.
 473: - **`409 nonce already used`** ג€” your code reused a nonce somehow; SDK generates fresh nonces per `send_to`, so this means you're calling `send_to` with cached envelope bytes. Rebuild.
 474: - **`429 rate limited`** ג€” back off + retry per `Retry-After` header.
 475: - **`410 plugin missing, revoked, not live-type, or not owned by sender`** (cards upsert) ג€” the plugin row's `card_type` isn't `"live"`, or the row has a non-null `revoked_at`, or the publish row's `sender_id` doesn't match the signed envelope's sender. The error message is intentionally generic so a probing caller can't distinguish the cases (don't leak which plugin UUIDs exist).
 476: - **`410 no active pairing`** (cards upsert) ג€” the recipient user has not paired with your sender, or the pairing has been revoked. The user needs to re-scan your pairing QR.
 477: - **`400 expires_at exceeds the 48h live-card cap`** (cards upsert) ג€” your supplied `expires_at` is more than 48 hours from now. Live cards are capped server-side to prevent slot squatting. Send shorter and re-upsert to extend.
 478: - **`400 expires_at is not in the future`** (cards upsert) ג€” you sent an already-expired `expires_at`. Use a future timestamp.
 479: - **`409 sequence_number not greater than existing`** (cards upsert) ג€” the existing card has a `sequence_number` ג‰¥ what you sent. Sequence must be strictly increasing per `card_key`.
 480: - **Card shows "render failed: plugin did not install __syncler_internal_dispatch ג€” missing registerPlugin() call?"** ג€” your bundle defined the plugin class but didn't call `registerPlugin(new YourPlugin())` at module scope. See ֲ§3.
 481: - **Card shows "endpoint not declared"** ג€” your `onclick` handler is calling a URL that doesn't match any pattern in your manifest's `declaredEndpoints`. Add the URL pattern (globs allowed: `https://example.com/api/*`) and re-publish.
 482: - **`HostPreviewValidationError: hostPreview.X is N UTF-8 bytes; max is M`** ג€” caught at `client.send_to` time. Trim the offending field; see ֲ§2 for the caps. UTF-8 byte counts, not characters ג€” emoji and accented characters cost more than one byte.
 483: - **Row shows "New message from {sender}" with fallback text only** ג€” your message was sent without a `hostPreview` block, or the block was malformed (logged + ignored on the device). The detail view still loads the plugin and renders normally; only the row is generic. Add a valid `hostPreview` and re-send.
 484: 
 485: Cross-reference `docs/crypto-spec.md` for the AAD + envelope canonical byte shapes if signatures disagree.

 succeeded in 287ms:
   1: # Syncler integration guide
   2: 
   3: You are integrating your app with the Syncler platform. Syncler is a content-blind transport + plugin host: your backend pushes end-to-end-encrypted blobs to a user's phone, and your plugin renders them. **Read this end-to-end before writing code; it's ~9 pages.**
   4: 
   5: Syncler does not know what your data looks like, what your UI says, or what your buttons do. Your payload, your plugin code (or template manifest), your callback endpoint ג€” Syncler just routes bytes.
   6: 
   7: ## 1. What you're building
   8: 
   9: You pick one of two render modes when you publish:
  10: 
  11: - **Script** (`renderer: "script"`) ג€” a JavaScript bundle running inside a sandboxed WebView. Maximum flexibility; you ship a `render(payload)` function that returns HTML. Buttons POST through `platform.network.fetch`.
  12: - **Template** (`renderer: "template"`) ג€” no JavaScript. You ship a small JSON manifest that maps fields out of your payload via JSONPath (`$.title`, `$.body.summary`) into a native Material 3 card. Buttons are host-rendered and the host POSTs the decrypted payload to the action's declared endpoint. Faster, lighter, no JS attack surface; constrained to a fixed set of layouts.
  13: 
  14: And one of two delivery modes:
  15: 
  16: - **Event** (`card_type: "event"`) ג€” the default. Each `send_to` produces a new immutable inbox row. Good for notifications, alerts, transactional events.
  17: - **Live** (`card_type: "live"`) ג€” persistent, upsertable. Subsequent upserts to the same `card_key` replace the previous payload (highest `sequence_number` wins). Good for status cards that change over time (delivery progress, market position, sensor reading). Server-enforced 48h TTL; you re-upsert to extend.
  18: 
  19: In every case you also need **backend code** that publishes the plugin once and sends payloads on demand, plus (for script renderer) an HTTP endpoint that receives the action callback.
  20: 
  21: The Syncler inbox shows a *native* row for every message ג€” sender name, title, subtitle, summary, arrival time ג€” pulled from the `hostPreview` block you embed in your payload (ֲ§2). The detail view that opens on tap is what your script bundle's `render()` or your template manifest produces.
  22: 
  23: ### What the host does for you
  24: 
  25: Once a card is in a user's inbox, the host handles all of the following without you doing anything plugin-side:
  26: 
  27: - **Native row rendering** from your `hostPreview` block (title / subtitle / summary) plus the server's arrival time (HH:mm for today, MMM d for older).
  28: - **Unread indicator** + read sync across the user's devices. A row marks read when the user opens the detail view; the state syncs via an encrypted CAS state blob.
  29: - **Left navigation drawer** with selectable views: **Unread** (only items the user hasn't opened), **All** (the default), **Archive** (items the user moved out of the main flow), and **Groups** ג€” an expandable list of every paired sender that lets the user filter the inbox down to one sender at a time. The top-bar title reflects the active view.
  30: - **Inbox search** (case-insensitive substring) over title, subtitle, summary, sender name, AND any tokens you supplied in `hostPreview.searchText`.
  31: - **Archive** + **Delete** + **Multi-select** with bulk Archive / Delete. Archive/delete state is local and synced across devices; deleted messages are hidden from inbox AND archive. The server retains messages until their normal expiry.
  32: - **Mute sync** ג€” the user can mute your plugin globally (all devices) or locally (this device only) from the host-owned settings sheet. Muted plugins are hidden from the active inbox but remain accessible in the Senders tab for unmuting.
  33: - **Bottom navigation** (Inbox / Senders / Settings) ג€” the user is always one tap away from your card.
  34: - **Revocation UX** ג€” if you revoke a plugin version with a `compromised` reason, the host refuses to execute the bundle on the device and shows a security banner instead. See ֲ§5.5.
  35: - **Live cards pin above events.** When mixed in the same inbox, live cards (`card_type: "live"`) sort above event cards (`card_type: "event"`), each subsorted by recency. The "Live" view in the drawer shows only live cards.
  36: - **Cross-device dismiss.** When the user dismisses a message on device A, the server marks `DeliveryStatus.dismissed_at` for that device. Device B's next inbox pull (driven by the `dismiss` SSE event or a fresh refresh) excludes the dismissed row ג€” `inbox_for_device` LEFT JOINs `DeliveryStatus` and filters `dismissed_at IS NULL`. Per-device dismiss, server-side.
  37: - **Real-time hints over SSE.** Foreground devices keep an authenticated Server-Sent Events stream open to `/v1/events`. The server pushes content-blind hints ג€” `inbox.changed`, `state.changed`, `dismiss`, `card.upsert`, `card.delete` ג€” and the client re-fetches over REST in response. The actual payloads still flow over the existing pull endpoints; SSE is the wakeup signal, not the data channel. Backgrounded devices fall back to FCM.
  38: 
  39: You don't need to opt into any of these. Populate `hostPreview` and they all work.
  40: 
  41: ## 2. Protocol
  42: 
  43: ### Payload (your backend -> user device)
  44: 
  45: Two parts: a reserved **`hostPreview`** block the platform renders natively as the inbox row, and the rest of the payload that your plugin's `render()` consumes for the detail view.
  46: 
  47: ```json
  48: {
  49:   "hostPreview": {
  50:     "title": "Something happened",
  51:     "subtitle": "Account A ג€¢ 12 minutes ago",
  52:     "summary": "Brief one-sentence context for the row.",
  53:     "searchText": ["account-a", "alert", "threshold"]
  54:   },
  55:   "item_id": "<your-internal-id>",
  56:   "body": "Details for the detail view, used by render()",
  57:   "action_label": "Acknowledge"
  58: }
  59: ```
  60: 
  61: That JSON is your `payload` argument to `client.send_to(...)`. The plugin's `render(payload)` receives the entire dict ג€” including the `hostPreview` block ג€” but it doesn't need to use it (the host already drew the row).
  62: 
  63: **`hostPreview` contract** (validated by `client.send_to` ג€” invalid blocks raise at send time):
  64: 
  65: | Field | Required | Type | Cap |
  66: |---|---|---|---|
  67: | `title` | yes | string | 80 UTF-8 bytes |
  68: | `subtitle` | no | string | 120 UTF-8 bytes |
  69: | `summary` | no | string | 240 UTF-8 bytes |
  70: | `searchText` | no | string[] | 16 entries x 64 UTF-8 bytes each |
  71: 
  72: Total serialized `hostPreview` <= 2048 UTF-8 bytes. Missing block -> the row falls back to *"New message from {sender_name}"*. Senders **should** include it.
  73: 
  74: `searchText` is folded into the host's inbox search alongside title, subtitle, summary, and sender name. The host does a case-insensitive substring match ג€” populate this with the terms a user would type into the search box but that aren't part of the visible row (ticker symbols, ticket numbers, account references). Plugin-scoped *content* search (a search bar that runs against your backend) is V1.5.
  75: 
  76: ### Action callback (user -> your backend)
  77: 
  78: When the user taps an action button in your plugin, the plugin POSTs to your declared endpoint with whatever body your `onclick` handler builds:
  79: 
  80: ```
  81: POST https://your-app.example.com/api/action
  82: Content-Type: application/json
  83: 
  84: {
  85:   "item_id": "...",
  86:   "acted_at": "2026-05-20T14:30:00Z"
  87: }
  88: ```
  89: 
  90: The platform does **not** inject `device_id` into the body in V1 ג€” see ֲ§7 for the full contract. Idempotency is your responsibility: dedupe by `item_id` (or a sender-generated identifier you echo back) because the platform may double-deliver under retry.

 240: @router.post("/{message_id}/dismiss", status_code=status.HTTP_204_NO_CONTENT)

 242:     message_id: uuid.UUID,
 243:     ctx: AuthContext = Depends(current_auth_context),
 244:     db: AsyncSession = Depends(get_db),
 245: ) -> Response:
 246:     # Device comes from the JWT ׳’ג‚¬ג€ no query param, no ownership check (the
 247:     # auth dependency already verified the device exists, belongs to the
 248:     # user, and is not revoked).
 249:     try:
 250:         message = await get_message_for_user(db, user_id=ctx.user.id, message_id=message_id)
 251:     except MessageNotFoundError as exc:
 252:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_404_NOT_FOUND, detail="message not found") from exc
 253:

 255:         await mark_dismissed(db, message_id=message_id, device_id=ctx.device.id)
 256:     except MessageNotFoundError as exc:

 258: 
 259:     # Fan out the dismiss event to other devices. The plugin's dismissBehavior
 260:     # is encoded on the device side (in the plugin manifest), but the platform
 261:     # always sends the event ׳’ג‚¬ג€ devices decide locally whether to act on it.
 262:     await push_dismiss_to_other_devices(db, message=message, dismissing_device_id=ctx.device.id)
 263:     # SSE hint: nudge OTHER foreground devices to update their local
 264:     # dismiss state. The dismissing device knows already; we mark its id
 265:     # so the client-side handler can no-op for self-originated events.
 266:     await get_event_bus().publish_to_user(
 267:         user_id=ctx.user.id,
 268:         event_type="dismiss",
 269:         data={"message_id": str(message_id), "source_device_id": str(ctx.device.id)},
 270:     )
 271:     return Response(status_code=status.HTTP_204_NO_CONTENT)

  23: async def check_rate_limit(db: AsyncSession, request: Request, config: RateLimitConfig) -> None:
  24:     now = datetime.now(UTC)
  25:     window_epoch = int(now.timestamp()) // config.window_seconds * config.window_seconds
  26:     window_start = datetime.fromtimestamp(window_epoch, UTC)
  27:     actor_type, actor_id = _identify_actor(config.name, request)

 140: def _identify_actor(name: str, request: Request) -> tuple[str, str]:
 141:     if name in {"login", "signup", "message_send_ip", "card_upsert_ip"}:
 142:         return "ip", _client_ip(request)
 143: 
 144:     if name in {"pairing_initiate", "message_send", "plugin_publish"}:
 145:         return "sender", _required_actor_value(request, "sender_id", "X-Sender-ID")
 146: 
 147:     if name == "message_send_user_hour":
 148:         sender_id = _required_actor_value(request, "sender_id", "X-Sender-ID")
 149:         user_id = _state_or_request_value(request, "user_id", "X-User-ID")
 150:         if user_id is None:
 151:             raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_400_BAD_REQUEST, detail="missing rate limit actor")
 152:         return "sender_user", f"{sender_id}:{user_id}"
 153: 
 154:     if name == "card_upsert":
 155:         sender_id = _required_actor_value(request, "sender_id", "X-Sender-ID")
 156:         user_id = _required_actor_value(request, "user_id", "X-User-ID")
 157:         card_key = _required_actor_value(request, "card_key", "X-Card-Key")
 158:         return "card", f"{sender_id}:{user_id}:{card_key}"
 159: 
 160:     if name == "manifest_fetch":
 161:         # `/v1/plugins/{sender_id}/{plugin_identifier}/latest` is unauthenticated
 162:         # (devices don't carry a session token on this lookup), so we key the
 163:         # bucket off the sender_id path param ג€” protects each sender's catalog
 164:         # from being hammered without requiring callers to advertise a device id.
 165:         return "sender", _required_actor_value(request, "sender_id", "X-Sender-ID")
 166: 
 167:     if name == "action_callback":
 168:         return "pairing", _required_actor_value(request, "pairing_id", "X-Pairing-ID")
 169: 
 170:     user_id = getattr(request.state, "user_id", None)
 171:     if user_id is not None:
 172:         return "user", str(user_id)
 173:     return "ip", _client_ip(request)
 174: 
 175: 
 176: def _required_actor_value(request: Request, path_param: str, header: str) -> str:
 177:     value = _state_or_request_value(request, path_param, header)
 178:     if value is None:
 179:         raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_400_BAD_REQUEST, detail="missing rate limit actor")
 180:     return value
 181: 
 182: 
 183: def _state_or_request_value(request: Request, path_param: str, header: str) -> str | None:
 184:     state_value = getattr(request.state, path_param, None)
 185:     if state_value is not None:
 186:         return str(state_value)
 187: 
 188:     path_value: Any = request.path_params.get(path_param)
 189:     if path_value is not None:
 190:         return str(path_value)
 191: 
 192:     header_value = request.headers.get(header)
 193:     if header_value:
 194:         return header_value
 195: 
 196:     return None
 197: 
 198: 
 199: def _client_ip(request: Request) -> str:
 200:     forwarded_for = request.headers.get("x-forwarded-for")
 201:     if forwarded_for:
 202:         return forwarded_for.split(",", 1)[0].strip()
 203:     if request.client is None:
 204:         return "unknown"
 205:     return request.client.host

  30: def decrypt_message_body(pairing_key: bytes, wire: bytes, aad: bytes) -> bytes:
  31:     """Decrypt a packed AES-GCM message body."""
  32: 
  33:     if len(pairing_key) != AES_256_KEY_BYTES:
  34:         raise ValueError("pairing_key must be 32 bytes")
  35:     if len(wire) < AES_GCM_NONCE_BYTES + AES_GCM_TAG_BYTES:
  36:         raise ValueError("wire is too short")
  37: 
  38:     nonce = wire[:AES_GCM_NONCE_BYTES]
  39:     ciphertext_with_tag = wire[AES_GCM_NONCE_BYTES:]
  40:     return AESGCM(pairing_key).decrypt(nonce, ciphertext_with_tag, aad)
  41: 
  42: 
  43: def assemble_aad(fields: dict[str, Any]) -> bytes:
  44:     """Assemble canonical JSON AAD for AES-GCM encryption.
  45: 
  46:     AAD authenticates the protocol context bound to the ciphertext but does
  47:     NOT include the ciphertext itself. See ``assemble_envelope`` for the
  48:     Ed25519 signing input.
  49:     """
  50:     return _canonical(fields)
  51: 
  52: 
  53: def assemble_envelope(fields: dict[str, Any]) -> bytes:
  54:     """Assemble canonical envelope JSON for Ed25519 sender signing.
  55: 
  56:     Envelope = AAD + ``encrypted_body`` (base64) + ``nonce`` (base64).
  57:     """
  58:     return _canonical(fields)
  59: 
  60: 
  61: def _canonical(fields: dict[str, Any]) -> bytes:
  62:     return json.dumps(
  63:         fields,
  64:         ensure_ascii=True,
  65:         separators=(",", ":"),
  66:         sort_keys=True,

  16: # Semver-lite: MAJOR.MINOR.PATCH[-prerelease]. Reject anything weirder.
  17: # Components capped at 6 digits each so server + client Int parsers agree.
  18: _SEMVER = re.compile(r"^(\d{1,6})\.(\d{1,6})\.(\d{1,6})(?:-[A-Za-z0-9.\-]+)?$")
  19: 
  20: 
  21: class PluginError(Exception):
  22:     """Base."""
  23: 
  24: 
  25: class InvalidVersionError(PluginError):
  26:     """Version string is not valid semver-lite."""
  27: 
  28: 
  29: class VersionRegressionError(PluginError):
  30:     """New version is not strictly greater than the latest published."""
  31: 
  32: 
  33: class DuplicateVersionError(PluginError):
  34:     """(sender_id, plugin_identifier, version) already exists."""

  37: class InvalidTemplateError(PluginError):
  38:     """Template configuration is malformed or invalid."""

  41: class PluginNotFoundError(PluginError):
  42:     """No plugin with that identifier."""

  44: 
  45: def _validate_template(template: dict, declared_endpoints: list[str]) -> None:
  46:     layout = template.get("layout")
  47:     if layout != "standard_card":
  48:         raise InvalidTemplateError(f"unknown or missing layout: {layout}")
  49: 
  50:     fields = template.get("fields", {})
  51:     if not isinstance(fields, dict):
  52:         raise InvalidTemplateError("fields must be a dictionary")
  53: 
  54:     if "title" not in fields:
  55:         raise InvalidTemplateError("missing required field: title")
  56: 
  57:     for name, config in fields.items():
  58:         if not isinstance(config, dict) or "path" not in config:
  59:             raise InvalidTemplateError(f"malformed config for field {name}")
  60:         path = config["path"]
  61:         if not isinstance(path, str) or not path.startswith("$"):
  62:             raise InvalidTemplateError(f"invalid JSONPath for field {name}: {path}")
  63: 
  64:     actions = template.get("actions", [])
  65:     if not isinstance(actions, list):
  66:         raise InvalidTemplateError("actions must be a list")
  67: 
  68:     for action in actions:
  69:         if not isinstance(action, dict):
  70:             raise InvalidTemplateError("malformed action")
  71:         aid = action.get("id")
  72:         label = action.get("label")
  73:         endpoint = action.get("endpoint")
  74:         if not aid or not label or not endpoint:
  75:             raise InvalidTemplateError("actions must have id, label, and endpoint")
  76: 
  77:         if endpoint not in declared_endpoints:
  78:             if not any(endpoint.startswith(p.rstrip("*")) for p in declared_endpoints if p.endswith("*")):
  79:                 raise InvalidTemplateError(
  80:                     f"action endpoint {endpoint} not covered by declaredEndpoints"
  81:                 )
  82: 
  83: 
  84: def _parse_version(version: str) -> tuple[int, int, int, str]:
  85:     match = _SEMVER.match(version)
  86:     if not match:
  87:         raise InvalidVersionError(f"invalid version: {version}")
  88:     major, minor, patch = (int(g) for g in match.groups()[:3])
  89:     pre = match.group(0).partition("-")[2] or "~"  # "~" sorts after any prerelease
  90:     return major, minor, patch, pre

  92: 
  93: async def publish_plugin(
  94:     db: AsyncSession,
  95:     *,
  96:     sender_id: uuid.UUID,
  97:     plugin_identifier: str,
  98:     version: str,
  99:     manifest_hash: bytes,
 100:     bundle_hash: bytes,
 101:     signature: bytes,
 102:     signed_bundle_url: str,
 103:     capabilities: list[str],
 104:     endpoints: list[str],
 105:     renderer: str = "script",
 106:     template: dict | None = None,
 107:     card_type: str = "event",
 108:     card_key_path: str | None = None,
 109: ) -> Plugin:
 110:     new_key = _parse_version(version)
 111: 
 112:     if renderer == "template":
 113:         if not template:
 114:             raise InvalidTemplateError("template object is required for renderer='template'")
 115:         _validate_template(template, endpoints)
 116:     elif renderer != "script":
 117:         raise InvalidTemplateError(f"unknown renderer type: {renderer}")
 118: 
 119:     if card_type == "live":
 120:         if not card_key_path:
 121:             raise InvalidTemplateError("card_key_path is required for card_type='live'")
 122:         if not card_key_path.startswith("$"):
 123:             raise InvalidTemplateError(f"invalid JSONPath for card_key_path: {card_key_path}")
 124:     elif card_type != "event":
 125:         raise InvalidTemplateError(f"unknown card_type: {card_type}")
 126: 
 127:     # Reject if any existing non-revoked version is >= new version.
 128:     existing = await db.execute(
 129:         select(Plugin).where(
 130:             and_(
 131:                 Plugin.sender_id == sender_id,
 132:                 Plugin.plugin_identifier == plugin_identifier,
 133:             ),
 134:         ),
 135:     )
 136:     for row in existing.scalars().all():
 137:         if _parse_version(row.version) >= new_key:
 138:             raise VersionRegressionError(
 139:                 f"new version {version} not greater than existing {row.version}",
 140:             )
 141: 
 142:     plugin = Plugin(
 143:         id=uuid.uuid4(),  # fresh row UUID per published version
 144:         sender_id=sender_id,
 145:         plugin_identifier=plugin_identifier,
 146:         version=version,
 147:         manifest_hash=manifest_hash,
 148:         bundle_hash=bundle_hash,
 149:         signature=signature,
 150:         signed_bundle_url=signed_bundle_url,
 151:         renderer=renderer,
 152:         template=template,
 153:         card_type=card_type,
 154:         card_key_path=card_key_path,
 155:         capabilities=capabilities,
 156:         endpoints=endpoints,
 157:     )
 158:     db.add(plugin)
 159:     try:
 160:         await db.commit()
 161:     except IntegrityError as exc:
 162:         await db.rollback()
 163:         msg = str(exc.orig) if exc.orig else str(exc)
 164:         if "uq_plugins_sender_identifier_version" in msg:
 165:             raise DuplicateVersionError(
 166:                 f"plugin {plugin_identifier} version {version} already exists",
 167:             ) from exc
 168:         raise
 169:     await db.refresh(plugin)
 170:     return plugin
 171: 
 172: 
 173: async def get_latest_for_plugin(
 174:     db: AsyncSession, *, sender_id: uuid.UUID, plugin_identifier: str
 175: ) -> Plugin:
 176:     result = await db.execute(
 177:         select(Plugin).where(
 178:             and_(
 179:                 Plugin.sender_id == sender_id,
 180:                 Plugin.plugin_identifier == plugin_identifier,
 181:                 Plugin.revoked_at.is_(None),
 182:             ),
 183:         ),
 184:     )
 185:     rows = list(result.scalars().all())
 186:     if not rows:
 187:         raise PluginNotFoundError(f"no active plugin {plugin_identifier} for sender")
 188:     rows.sort(key=lambda r: _parse_version(r.version), reverse=True)
 189:     return rows[0]
 190: 
 191: 
 192: async def get_plugin_by_id(
 193:     db: AsyncSession, *, plugin_row_id: uuid.UUID
 194: ) -> Plugin:
 195:     result = await db.execute(select(Plugin).where(Plugin.id == plugin_row_id))
 196:     plugin = result.scalar_one_or_none()
 197:     if plugin is None:
 198:         raise PluginNotFoundError(f"no plugin row {plugin_row_id}")
 199:     return plugin

 148: def load_private_key(path: str) -> Ed25519PrivateKey:
 149:     """Load an Ed25519 private key from a PEM file. Generate one if absent."""
 150:     expanded = os.path.expanduser(path)
 151:     if not os.path.exists(expanded):
 152:         return generate_and_save_private_key(expanded)
 153:     with open(expanded, "rb") as f:
 154:         data = f.read()
 155:     return serialization.load_pem_private_key(data, password=None)
 156: 
 157: 
 158: def generate_and_save_private_key(path: str) -> Ed25519PrivateKey:
 159:     key = Ed25519PrivateKey.generate()
 160:     pem = key.private_bytes(
 161:         encoding=serialization.Encoding.PEM,
 162:         format=serialization.PrivateFormat.PKCS8,
 163:         encryption_algorithm=serialization.NoEncryption(),
 164:     )
 165:     os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(path) or ".", exist_ok=True)
 166:     with open(path, "wb") as f:
 167:         f.write(pem)
 168:     os.chmod(path, 0o600)
 169:     return key
 170: 
 171: 
 172: def public_key_raw(key: Ed25519PrivateKey) -> bytes:
 173:     return key.public_key().public_bytes(
 174:         encoding=serialization.Encoding.Raw,
 175:         format=serialization.PublicFormat.Raw,
 176:     )
 177:

 179: def encrypt_payload(
 180:     *,
 181:     pairing_key: bytes,
 182:     plaintext: bytes,
 183:     aad: bytes,
 184: ) -> tuple[bytes, bytes]:
 185:     """Returns (nonce, ciphertext_with_tag)."""
 186:     if len(pairing_key) != 32:
 187:         raise ValueError("pairing_key must be 32 bytes")
 188:     nonce = random_nonce()
 189:     ciphertext = AESGCM(pairing_key).encrypt(nonce, plaintext, aad)
 190:     return nonce, ciphertext

**Codex Reviewer Verdict**

`docs/integration-guide.md`: **RED**

Blocking mismatches:

- Broken live-card upsert example: `docs/integration-guide.md:316-336` imports `assemble_aad` but calls `assemble_live_card_aad`, and calls `encrypt_payload(client.pairing_key, nonce, plaintext, aad)` positionally. Actual SDK has `assemble_live_card_aad(...)` in `sdk-python/syncler/crypto.py:85-104`, and `encrypt_payload` is keyword-only, generates the nonce, and returns `(nonce, ciphertext)` at `sdk-python/syncler/crypto.py:179-190`.
- Rate limit is documented as “1 upsert per second” at `docs/integration-guide.md:357`, but code enforces fixed-window `60/min` per card: `server/app/middleware/rate_limit_config.py:27-29`, `server/app/middleware/rate_limit.py:23-44`.
- Cross-device dismiss mechanism is inaccurately described at `docs/integration-guide.md:36`. The server marks only the dismissing device’s `DeliveryStatus`: `server/app/routers/messages.py:254-270`, `server/app/services/messages.py:238-258`. The inbox filter is per-device: `server/app/services/messages.py:198-208`; a different device’s next pull is not excluded by that server-side join.
- `card_key_path` is described as a JSONPath at `docs/integration-guide.md:294`, but server validation only requires non-empty in schema and only `startswith("$")` in service: `server/app/schemas.py:571-574`, `server/app/services/plugins.py:119-123`.

Confirmed accurate:

- `publish_plugin(...)` signature/defaults match `sdk-python/syncler/client.py:294-345`.
- `delete_card(...)` requires `user_id`: `sdk-python/syncler/client.py:389-420`.
- `send_to(...)` shape/defaults and hostPreview validation match `sdk-python/syncler/client.py:208-290`, `sdk-python/syncler/preview.py:32-103`.
- Revoke reasons match `sdk-python/syncler/client.py:422-465`.
- Live-card 410/400/409 mappings match `server/app/routers/cards.py:109-122`.
- SSE event names match `android/core/network/.../EventStreamManager.kt:330-347`.
- Template action POST does not attach Authorization: `android/feature/inbox/.../TemplateCard.kt:187-231`.

`docs/crypto-spec.md`: **RED**

- The AAD JSON block claims sorted canonical JSON but is not in canonical sorted order: `docs/crypto-spec.md:228-237`. Actual canonical bytes sort keys via server `server/app/crypto/aead.py:61-67` and Android `android/core/crypto/.../Aad.kt:71-82`. Correct order is `card_key`, `card_type`, `expires_at`, `plugin_id`, `sender_id`, `sequence_number`, `user_id`.
- UUID canonicalization is required in prose at `docs/crypto-spec.md:262`, but the reference snippets use `str(value)` rather than `str(uuid.UUID(value))`: `docs/crypto-spec.md:322-324`, `350-353`, `369-370`. The SDK client normalizes in `sdk-python/syncler/client.py:367-383`, but the public copy-paste builders do not.

`docs/ROADMAP.md`: **YELLOW**

- `docs/ROADMAP.md:14` says “plugin revoke” in the host-owned settings sheet. The Android UI exposes “Revoke pairing,” not plugin-row revoke: `android/feature/inbox/.../PluginSettingsSheet.kt:192-203`, `android/feature/inbox/.../InboxRepository.kt:163-177`. Sender-side plugin revoke exists, but that is not host-owned user UX.

**Buildability Gaps**

A new author could not build a working template-renderer live-card plugin from the docs alone without guessing:

- The live-card encryption example does not run as written.
- There is no complete single example combining `renderer="template"` + `card_type="live"` + `card_key_path`.
- The live-card plaintext example lacks `hostPreview`, so the inbox row falls back despite the docs telling authors to populate it.
- The docs imply `card_key_path` drives merging, but current upsert uses the explicit `card_key` request field; authors need to know those must agree.

**Overall:** **hold**. The implementation is mostly aligned, but the public docs need fixes before they are safe as the contract.
